      <p>
       <b>
        Iraq
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ

            r
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'r' in 'rye'">
            r
           </span>
           <span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">
            ɑː
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="nowrap">
         (
         <span class="unicode haudio">
          <span class="fn">
           <span style="white-space:nowrap">
            <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Iraq.ogg" title="About this sound">
             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
            </a>
           </span>
           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cf/En-us-Iraq.ogg" title="En-us-Iraq.ogg">
            listen
           </a>
          </span>
         </span>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       or
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">
            aɪ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'r' in 'rye'">
            r
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
        Arabic
       </a>
       :
       <span dir="rtl" lang="ar">
        العراق
       </span>
       ‎
       <i>
        al-‘Irāq
       </i>
       ;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kurdish_language" title="Kurdish language">
        Kurdish
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span dir="rtl" lang="ku">
         عێراق
        </span>
       </i>
       ‎
       <i>
        Eraq
       </i>
       ), officially known as the
       <b>
        Republic of Iraq
       </b>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
        Arabic
       </a>
       :
       <span dir="rtl" lang="ar">
        جُمُهورية العِراق
       </span>
       ‎
       <i>
        <span class="unicode haudio">
         <span class="fn">
          <span style="white-space:nowrap">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Ar-Jumh%C5%ABriyyat_al-%E2%80%98Ir%C4%81q.oga" title="About this sound">
            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3a/Ar-Jumh%C5%ABriyyat_al-%E2%80%98Ir%C4%81q.oga" title="Ar-Jumhūriyyat al-‘Irāq.oga">
           Jumhūrīyyat al-‘Irāq
          </a>
         </span>
        </span>
       </i>
       ;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kurdish_language" title="Kurdish language">
        Kurdish
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span dir="rtl" lang="ku">
         کۆماری عێراق
        </span>
       </i>
       ‎
       <i>
        Komari Eraq
       </i>
       ), is a country in
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">
        Western Asia
       </a>
       , bordered by
       <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
        Turkey
       </a>
       to the north,
       <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">
        Iran
       </a>
       to the east,
       <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">
        Kuwait
       </a>
       to the southeast,
       <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">
        Saudi Arabia
       </a>
       to the south,
       <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">
        Jordan
       </a>
       to the southwest and
       <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
        Syria
       </a>
       to the west. The capital, and largest city, is
       <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">
        Baghdad
       </a>
       . The main ethnic groups are
       <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">
        Arabs
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Kurds" title="Kurds">
        Kurds
       </a>
       ; others include
       <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">
        Assyrians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Turkmens" title="Iraqi Turkmens">
        Turkmen
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Shabak_people" title="Shabak people">
        Shabakis
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Yazidis" title="Yazidis">
        Yazidis
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Iraq" title="Armenians in Iraq">
        Armenians
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mandeans" title="Mandeans">
        Mandeans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Circassians_in_Iraq" title="Circassians in Iraq">
        Circassians
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kawliya" title="Kawliya">
        Kawliya
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Around 95% of the country's 37 million citizens are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">
        Muslims
       </a>
       , with
       <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
        Christianity
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yarsan" title="Yarsan">
        Yarsan
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yezidism" title="Yezidism">
        Yezidism
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mandeanism" title="Mandeanism">
        Mandeanism
       </a>
       also present. The official languages of Iraq are
       <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">
        Arabic
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_languages" title="Kurdish languages">
        Kurdish
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Iraq has a coastline measuring 58 km (36 miles) on the northern
       <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">
        Persian Gulf
       </a>
       and encompasses the
       <a href="/wiki/Tigris%E2%80%93Euphrates_river_system" title="Tigris–Euphrates river system">
        Mesopotamian Alluvial Plain
       </a>
       , the northwestern end of the
       <a href="/wiki/Zagros_Mountains" title="Zagros Mountains">
        Zagros mountain range
       </a>
       and the eastern part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Desert" title="Syrian Desert">
        Syrian Desert
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Two major rivers, the
       <a href="/wiki/Tigris" title="Tigris">
        Tigris
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Euphrates" title="Euphrates">
        Euphrates
       </a>
       , run south through Iraq and into the
       <a href="/wiki/Shatt_al-Arab" title="Shatt al-Arab">
        Shatt al-Arab
       </a>
       near the
       <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">
        Persian Gulf
       </a>
       . These rivers provide Iraq with significant amounts of fertile land.
      </p>
      <p>
       The region between the
       <a href="/wiki/Tigris%E2%80%93Euphrates_river_system" title="Tigris–Euphrates river system">
        Tigris and Euphrates rivers
       </a>
       , historically known as
       <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">
        Mesopotamia
       </a>
       , is often referred to as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cradle_of_civilisation" title="Cradle of civilisation">
        cradle of civilisation
       </a>
       . It was here that mankind first began to read, write, create laws and live in cities under an organised government—notably
       <a href="/wiki/Uruk" title="Uruk">
        Uruk
       </a>
       , from which "Iraq" is derived. The area has been home to successive civilisations since the
       <a href="/wiki/6th_millennium_BC" title="6th millennium BC">
        6th millennium BC
       </a>
       . Iraq was the centre of the
       <a href="/wiki/Akkadian_Empire" title="Akkadian Empire">
        Akkadian
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-Sumerian_Empire" title="Neo-Sumerian Empire">
        Sumerian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Neo-Assyrian_Empire" title="Neo-Assyrian Empire">
        Assyrian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Neo-Babylonian_Empire" title="Neo-Babylonian Empire">
        Babylonian
       </a>
       empires. It was also part of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Median_Empire" title="Median Empire">
        Median
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Assyria" title="Achaemenid Assyria">
        Achaemenid
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">
        Hellenistic
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arsacid_Empire" title="Arsacid Empire">
        Parthian
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanid_Empire" title="Sassanid Empire">
        Sassanid
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate" title="Rashidun Caliphate">
        Rashidun
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">
        Umayyad
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">
        Abbasid
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ayyubid_dynasty" title="Ayyubid dynasty">
        Ayyubid
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ilkhanate" title="Ilkhanate">
        Mongol
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Safavid_Empire" title="Safavid Empire">
        Safavid
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Afsharid_dynasty" title="Afsharid dynasty">
        Afsharid
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman
       </a>
       empires.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Iraq's modern borders were mostly demarcated in 1920 by the
       <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">
        League of Nations
       </a>
       when the
       <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Partition of the Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman Empire was divided
       </a>
       by the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres" title="Treaty of Sèvres">
        Treaty of Sèvres
       </a>
       . Iraq was placed under the authority of the United Kingdom as the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Mandate_for_Mesopotamia_(legal_instrument)" title="British Mandate for Mesopotamia (legal instrument)">
        British Mandate of Mesopotamia
       </a>
       . A monarchy was established in 1921, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Iraq" title="Kingdom of Iraq">
        Kingdom of Iraq
       </a>
       gained independence from Britain in 1932. In 1958,
       <a href="/wiki/14_July_Revolution" title="14 July Revolution">
        the monarchy was overthrown
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Republic_(1958%E2%80%9368)" title="Iraqi Republic (1958–68)">
        Iraqi Republic
       </a>
       created. Iraq was controlled by the
       <a href="/wiki/Ba%27ath_Party_(Iraqi-dominated_faction)" title="Ba'ath Party (Iraqi-dominated faction)">
        Arab Socialist Ba'ath Party
       </a>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/Ba%27athist_Iraq" title="Ba'athist Iraq">
        1968 until 2003
       </a>
       . After
       <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">
        an invasion
       </a>
       by the United States and
       <a href="/wiki/Multi-National_Force_%E2%80%93_Iraq" title="Multi-National Force – Iraq">
        its allies
       </a>
       in 2003,
       <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">
        Saddam Hussein
       </a>
       's Ba'ath Party was removed from power, and multi-party
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_parliamentary_election,_December_2005" title="Iraqi parliamentary election, December 2005">
        parliamentary elections were held in 2005
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">
        American presence in Iraq
       </a>
       ended in 2011,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn-dec11_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cnn-dec11-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but the
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_insurgency_(2011%E2%80%9313)" title="Iraqi insurgency (2011–13)">
        Iraqi insurgency
       </a>
       continued and intensified as fighters from the
       <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" title="Syrian Civil War">
        Syrian Civil War
       </a>
       spilled into the country. Out of the insurgency came a highly destructive group calling itself
       <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">
        ISIL
       </a>
       , which took large parts of the north and west. It has since been largely defeated. Disputes over the sovereignty of
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Kurdistan" title="Iraqi Kurdistan">
        Iraqi Kurdistan
       </a>
       continue. A
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Kurdistan_independence_referendum,_2017" title="Iraqi Kurdistan independence referendum, 2017">
        referendum
       </a>
       about the full sovereignty of Iraqi Kurdistan was held on 25 September 2017.
      </p>
      <p>
       Iraq is a founding member of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        UN
       </a>
       as well as of the
       <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">
        Arab League
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organization_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organization of Islamic Cooperation">
        OIC
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">
        Non-Aligned Movement
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">
        IMF
       </a>
       . It is a
       <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">
        federal
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">
        parliamentary
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">
        republic
       </a>
       consisting of
       <a href="/wiki/Governorates_of_Iraq" title="Governorates of Iraq">
        19 governorates (provinces)
       </a>
       and one autonomous region (
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Kurdistan" title="Iraqi Kurdistan">
        Iraqi Kurdistan
       </a>
       ). The country's official religion is
       <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Iraq" title="Islam in Iraq">
        Islam
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Iraq" title="Culture of Iraq">
        Culturally
       </a>
       , Iraq has a very rich heritage and celebrates the achievements of its past in pre-Islamic times and is known for its poets. Its painters and sculptors are among the best in the
       <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">
        Arab world
       </a>
       , some of them being world-class as well as producing fine handicrafts, including rugs and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carpets" title="Carpets">
        carpets
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Name">
        Name
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       <span id="Etymology">
       </span>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">
        Arabic
       </a>
       name
       <span lang="ar">
        العراق
       </span>
       <i>
        al-ʿIrāq
       </i>
       has been in use since before the 6th century. There are several suggested origins for the name. One dates to the
       <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">
        Sumerian
       </a>
       city of
       <a href="/wiki/Uruk" title="Uruk">
        Uruk
       </a>
       (Biblical Hebrew
       <i>
        Erech
       </i>
       ) and is thus ultimately of
       <a href="/wiki/Sumerian_language" title="Sumerian language">
        Sumerian
       </a>
       origin, as
       <i>
        Uruk
       </i>
       was the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akkadian_language" title="Akkadian language">
        Akkadian
       </a>
       name for the Sumerian city of
       <i>
        <span lang="sux-Latn">
         Urug
        </span>
       </i>
       , containing the Sumerian word for "city",
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cities_of_the_ancient_Near_East" title="Cities of the ancient Near East">
        UR
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       An Arabic folk etymology for the name is "deeply rooted, well-watered;
       <a href="/wiki/Fertile_Crescent" title="Fertile Crescent">
        fertile
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the medieval period, there was a region called
       <i>
        ʿIrāq ʿArabī
       </i>
       ("Arabian Iraq") for Lower
       <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">
        Mesopotamia
       </a>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Persian_Iraq" title="Persian Iraq">
         ʿIrāq ʿajamī
        </a>
       </i>
       ("Foreign Iraq"),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       for the region now situated in Central and Western Iran.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ʿERĀQ-EʿAJAMĪ_Persian_Iraq_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ʿERĀQ-EʿAJAMĪ_Persian_Iraq-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The term historically included the plain south of the
       <a href="/wiki/Hamrin_Mountains" title="Hamrin Mountains">
        Hamrin Mountains
       </a>
       and did not include the northernmost and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Jazira,_Mesopotamia" title="Al-Jazira, Mesopotamia">
        westernmost
       </a>
       parts of the modern territory of Iraq.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bernhardsson-97_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bernhardsson-97-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Prior to the middle of the 19th century, the term
       <b>
        Eyraca Arabic
       </b>
       was commonly used to describe Iraq.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The term
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Sawad" title="Sawad">
         Sawad
        </a>
       </i>
       was also used in early Islamic times for the region of the
       <a href="/wiki/Alluvial_plain" title="Alluvial plain">
        alluvial plain
       </a>
       of the Tigris and Euphrates rivers, contrasting it with the arid Arabian desert. As an Arabic word,
       <span lang="ar">
        عراق
       </span>
       means "hem", "shore", "bank", or "edge", so that the name by folk etymology came to be interpreted as "the
       <a href="/wiki/Escarpment" title="Escarpment">
        escarpment
       </a>
       ", viz. at the south and east of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Jazira,_Mesopotamia" title="Al-Jazira, Mesopotamia">
        Jazira
       </a>
       Plateau, which forms the northern and western edge of the "al-Iraq arabi" area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Arabic_phonology" title="Arabic phonology">
        Arabic pronunciation
       </a>
       is
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Arabic" title="Help:IPA/Arabic">
         [ʕiˈrɑːq]
        </a>
       </span>
       . In English, it is either
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'r' in 'rye'">
            r
           </span>
           <span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">
            ɑː
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       (the only pronunciation listed in the
       <a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">
        Oxford English Dictionary
       </a>
       and the first one in
       <a class="external text" href="http://merriam-webster.com/dictionary/iraq" rel="nofollow">
        Merriam-Webster's Online Dictionary
       </a>
       ) or
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'r' in 'rye'">
            r
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       (listed first by
       <a href="/wiki/Macquarie_Dictionary" title="Macquarie Dictionary">
        MQD
       </a>
       ), the
       <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20080314173050/http://www.bartleby.com/61/81/I0228100.html" rel="nofollow">
        American Heritage Dictionary
       </a>
       , and the
       <a class="external text" href="http://dictionary.infoplease.com/Iraq" rel="nofollow">
        Random House Dictionary
       </a>
       . The pronunciation
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">
            aɪ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'r' in 'rye'">
            r
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       is frequently heard in US media.
      </p>
      <p>
       In accordance with the 2005
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Iraq" title="Constitution of Iraq">
        Constitution
       </a>
       , the official name of the state is the
       <i>
        "Republic of Iraq"
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        Jumhūrīyyat al-‘Irāq
       </i>
       ).
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iraq" title="History of Iraq">
        History of Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-historic_era">
        Pre-historic era
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Between 65,000 BC and 35,000 BC northern Iraq was home to a
       <a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">
        Neanderthal
       </a>
       culture, archaeological remains of which have been discovered at
       <a href="/wiki/Shanidar_Cave" title="Shanidar Cave">
        Shanidar Cave
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This same region is also the location of a number of pre-Neolithic cemeteries, dating from approximately 11,000 BC.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ralph_S._Solecki_2004_pp._3_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ralph_S._Solecki_2004_pp._3-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Since approximately 10,000 BC, Iraq (alongside
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asia_Minor" title="Asia Minor">
        Asia Minor
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Levant" title="The Levant">
        The Levant
       </a>
       ) was one of centres of a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caucasoid" title="Caucasoid">
        Caucasoid
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">
        Neolithic
       </a>
       culture (known as
       <a href="/wiki/Pre-Pottery_Neolithic_A" title="Pre-Pottery Neolithic A">
        Pre-Pottery Neolithic A
       </a>
       ) where agriculture and cattle breeding appeared for the first time in the world. The following Neolithic period (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PPNB" title="PPNB">
        PPNB
       </a>
       ) is represented by rectangular houses. At the time of the pre-pottery Neolithic, people used vessels made of stone, gypsum and burnt lime (Vaisselle blanche). Finds of obsidian tools from Anatolia are evidences of early trade relations.
      </p>
      <p>
       Further important sites of human advancement were
       <a href="/wiki/Jarmo" title="Jarmo">
        Jarmo
       </a>
       (circa 7100 BC),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ralph_S._Solecki_2004_pp._3_18-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ralph_S._Solecki_2004_pp._3-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/Halaf_culture" title="Halaf culture">
        Halaf culture
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ubaid_period" title="Ubaid period">
        Ubaid period
       </a>
       (between 6500 BC and 3800 BC).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These periods show ever-increasing levels of advancement in agriculture, tool-making and architecture.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_Iraq">
        Ancient Iraq
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-one_source" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="Question book-new.svg" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           relies largely or entirely on a single
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">
            source
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Relevant discussion may be found on the
           <a href="/wiki/Talk:Iraq##" title="Talk:Iraq">
            talk page
           </a>
           . Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iraq&amp;action=edit">
            improve this article
           </a>
           by introducing
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
            citations
           </a>
           to additional sources.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (June 2014)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cylinder_Seal,_Old_Babylonian,_formerly_in_the_Charterhouse_Collection_09.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="978" data-file-width="1747" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Cylinder_Seal%2C_Old_Babylonian%2C_formerly_in_the_Charterhouse_Collection_09.jpg/320px-Cylinder_Seal%2C_Old_Babylonian%2C_formerly_in_the_Charterhouse_Collection_09.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Cylinder_Seal%2C_Old_Babylonian%2C_formerly_in_the_Charterhouse_Collection_09.jpg/480px-Cylinder_Seal%2C_Old_Babylonian%2C_formerly_in_the_Charterhouse_Collection_09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Cylinder_Seal%2C_Old_Babylonian%2C_formerly_in_the_Charterhouse_Collection_09.jpg/640px-Cylinder_Seal%2C_Old_Babylonian%2C_formerly_in_the_Charterhouse_Collection_09.jpg 2x" width="320"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cylinder_Seal,_Old_Babylonian,_formerly_in_the_Charterhouse_Collection_09.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cylinder_Seal" title="Cylinder Seal">
          Cylinder Seal
         </a>
         , Old Babylonian Period, c.1800 BC,
         <a href="/wiki/Hematite" title="Hematite">
          hematite
         </a>
         . The king makes an animal offering to
         <a href="/wiki/Shamash" title="Shamash">
          Shamash
         </a>
         . This seal was probably made in a workshop at
         <a href="/wiki/Sippar" title="Sippar">
          Sippar
         </a>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
          <a href="#cite_note-20">
           [20]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Mesopotamia" title="History of Mesopotamia">
        History of Mesopotamia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The historical period in Iraq truly begins during the
       <a href="/wiki/Uruk_period" title="Uruk period">
        Uruk period
       </a>
       (4000 BC to 3100 BC), with the founding of a number of
       <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">
        Sumerian
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cities" title="Cities">
        cities
       </a>
       , and the use of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pictographs" title="Pictographs">
        Pictographs
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cylinder_seals" title="Cylinder seals">
        Cylinder seals
       </a>
       and mass-produced goods.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cradle_of_Civilization" title="Cradle of Civilization">
        Cradle of Civilization
       </a>
       " is thus a common term for the area comprising modern Iraq as it was home to the earliest known
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civilisation" title="Civilisation">
        civilisation
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">
        Sumerian civilisation
       </a>
       , which arose in the fertile
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tigris-Euphrates_river_system" title="Tigris-Euphrates river system">
        Tigris-Euphrates river valley
       </a>
       of southern Iraq in the
       <a href="/wiki/Chalcolithic" title="Chalcolithic">
        Chalcolithic
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Ubaid_period" title="Ubaid period">
        Ubaid period
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       It was here, in the late
       <a href="/wiki/4th_millennium_BC" title="4th millennium BC">
        4th millennium BC
       </a>
       , that the world's
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_languages_by_first_written_accounts" title="List of languages by first written accounts">
        first
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Cuneiform_script" title="Cuneiform script">
        writing system
       </a>
       and recorded history itself were born. The
       <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">
        Sumerians
       </a>
       were also the first to harness the
       <a href="/wiki/Wheel" title="Wheel">
        wheel
       </a>
       and create
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_States" title="City States">
        City States
       </a>
       , and whose writings record the first evidence of
       <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">
        Mathematics
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">
        Astronomy
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Astrology" title="Astrology">
        Astrology
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Written_Law" title="Written Law">
        Written Law
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">
        Medicine
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organised_religion" title="Organised religion">
        Organised religion
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Sumerian_language" title="Sumerian language">
        language
       </a>
       of the Sumerians is a
       <a href="/wiki/Language_isolate" title="Language isolate">
        language isolate
       </a>
       . The major city states of the early Sumerian period were;
       <a href="/wiki/Eridu" title="Eridu">
        Eridu
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bad-tibira" title="Bad-tibira">
        Bad-tibira
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Larsa" title="Larsa">
        Larsa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sippar" title="Sippar">
        Sippar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Shuruppak" title="Shuruppak">
        Shuruppak
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Uruk" title="Uruk">
        Uruk
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kish_(Sumer)" title="Kish (Sumer)">
        Kish
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ur" title="Ur">
        Ur
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nippur" title="Nippur">
        Nippur
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lagash" title="Lagash">
        Lagash
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Girsu" title="Girsu">
        Girsu
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Umma" title="Umma">
        Umma
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hamazi" title="Hamazi">
        Hamazi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Adab_(city)" title="Adab (city)">
        Adab
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mari,_Syria" title="Mari, Syria">
        Mari
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Isin" title="Isin">
        Isin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kutha" title="Kutha">
        Kutha
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Der_(Sumer)" title="Der (Sumer)">
        Der
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Akshak" title="Akshak">
        Akshak
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The cities to the north like
       <a href="/wiki/Ashur" title="Ashur">
        Ashur
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arbil" title="Arbil">
        Arbela
       </a>
       (modern
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irbil" title="Irbil">
        Irbil
       </a>
       ) and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrapkha" title="Arrapkha">
        Arrapkha
       </a>
       (modern
       <a href="/wiki/Kirkuk" title="Kirkuk">
        Kirkuk
       </a>
       ) were also extant in what was to be called Assyria from the 25th century BC; however, at this early stage, they were Sumerian ruled administrative centres.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:P1150890_Louvre_st%C3%A8le_de_victoire_Akkad_AO2678_rwk.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1873" data-file-width="3000" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/P1150890_Louvre_st%C3%A8le_de_victoire_Akkad_AO2678_rwk.jpg/220px-P1150890_Louvre_st%C3%A8le_de_victoire_Akkad_AO2678_rwk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/P1150890_Louvre_st%C3%A8le_de_victoire_Akkad_AO2678_rwk.jpg/330px-P1150890_Louvre_st%C3%A8le_de_victoire_Akkad_AO2678_rwk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/P1150890_Louvre_st%C3%A8le_de_victoire_Akkad_AO2678_rwk.jpg/440px-P1150890_Louvre_st%C3%A8le_de_victoire_Akkad_AO2678_rwk.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:P1150890_Louvre_st%C3%A8le_de_victoire_Akkad_AO2678_rwk.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Victory stele of
         <a href="/wiki/Naram-Sin_of_Akkad" title="Naram-Sin of Akkad">
          Naram-Sin of Akkad
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bronze_Age">
        Bronze Age
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       In the 26th century BC,
       <a href="/wiki/Eannatum" title="Eannatum">
        Eannatum
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Lagash" title="Lagash">
        Lagash
       </a>
       created what was perhaps the first
       <a href="/wiki/Empire" title="Empire">
        empire
       </a>
       in history, though this was short-lived. Later,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lugal-Zage-Si" title="Lugal-Zage-Si">
        Lugal-Zage-Si
       </a>
       , the priest-king of
       <a href="/wiki/Umma" title="Umma">
        Umma
       </a>
       , overthrew the primacy of the Lagash dynasty in the area, then conquered
       <a href="/wiki/Uruk" title="Uruk">
        Uruk
       </a>
       , making it his capital, and claimed an empire extending from the
       <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">
        Persian Gulf
       </a>
       to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean" title="Mediterranean">
        Mediterranean
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was during this period that the
       <a href="/wiki/Epic_of_Gilgamesh" title="Epic of Gilgamesh">
        Epic of Gilgamesh
       </a>
       originates, which includes the tale of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Great_Flood" title="The Great Flood">
        The Great Flood
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       From the 29th century BC, Akkadian Semitic names began to appear on king lists and administrative documents of various city states. It remains unknown as to the origin of Akkad, where it was precisely situated and how it rose to prominence. Its people spoke
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akkadian_language" title="Akkadian language">
        Akkadian
       </a>
       , an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Semitic_language" title="East Semitic language">
        East Semitic language
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the 3rd millennium BC, a cultural symbiosis developed between the Sumerians and the Akkadians, which included widespread
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilingualism" title="Bilingualism">
        bilingualism
       </a>
       . The influences between
       <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">
        Sumerian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Akkadian" title="Akkadian">
        Akkadian
       </a>
       are evident in all areas, including lexical borrowing on a massive scale—and syntactic, morphological, and phonological convergence. This mutual influence has prompted scholars to refer to Sumerian and Akkadian of the 3rd millennium BC as a
       <a href="/wiki/Sprachbund" title="Sprachbund">
        Sprachbund
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       From this period, the civilisation in Iraq came to be known as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sumero-Akkadian" title="Sumero-Akkadian">
        Sumero-Akkadian
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bill_of_sale_Louvre_AO3765.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1650" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Bill_of_sale_Louvre_AO3765.jpg/220px-Bill_of_sale_Louvre_AO3765.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Bill_of_sale_Louvre_AO3765.jpg/330px-Bill_of_sale_Louvre_AO3765.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Bill_of_sale_Louvre_AO3765.jpg/440px-Bill_of_sale_Louvre_AO3765.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bill_of_sale_Louvre_AO3765.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Bill of sale of a male slave and a building in
         <a href="/wiki/Shuruppak" title="Shuruppak">
          Shuruppak
         </a>
         , Sumerian tablet, circa 2600 BC.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Between the 29th and 24th centuries BC, a number of kingdoms and city states within Iraq began to have Akkadian speaking dynasties; including
       <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">
        Assyria
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ekallatum" title="Ekallatum">
        Ekallatum
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Isin" title="Isin">
        Isin
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Larsa" title="Larsa">
        Larsa
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       However, the Sumerians remained generally dominant until the rise of the
       <a href="/wiki/Akkadian_Empire" title="Akkadian Empire">
        Akkadian Empire
       </a>
       (2335–2124 BC), based in the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Akkad_(city)" title="Akkad (city)">
        Akkad
       </a>
       in central Iraq.
       <a href="/wiki/Sargon_of_Akkad" title="Sargon of Akkad">
        Sargon of Akkad
       </a>
       , originally a
       <a href="/wiki/Rabshakeh" title="Rabshakeh">
        Rabshakeh
       </a>
       to a Sumerian king, founded the empire, he conquered all of the city states of southern and central Iraq, and subjugated the kings of Assyria, thus uniting the Sumerians and Akkadians in one state. He then set about expanding his empire, conquering
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gutium" title="Gutium">
        Gutium
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Elam" title="Elam">
        Elam
       </a>
       and had victories that did not result into a full conquest against the
       <a href="/wiki/Amorites" title="Amorites">
        Amorites
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ebla" title="Ebla">
        Eblaites
       </a>
       of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Syria" title="Ancient Syria">
        Ancient Syria
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       After the collapse of the Akkadian Empire in the late 22nd century BC, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gutians" title="Gutians">
        Gutians
       </a>
       occupied the south for a few decades, while Assyria reasserted its independence in the north. This was followed by a Sumerian renaissance in the form of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-Sumerian_Empire" title="Neo-Sumerian Empire">
        Neo-Sumerian Empire
       </a>
       . The Sumerians under king
       <a href="/wiki/Shulgi" title="Shulgi">
        Shulgi
       </a>
       conquered almost all of Iraq except the northern reaches of Assyria, and asserted themselves over the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gutians" title="Gutians">
        Gutians
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elamites" title="Elamites">
        Elamites
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Amorites" title="Amorites">
        Amorites
       </a>
       , destroying the first and holding off the others.
      </p>
      <p>
       An
       <a href="/wiki/Elam" title="Elam">
        Elamite
       </a>
       invasion in 2004 BC brought the Sumerian revival to an end. By the mid 21st century BC, the Akkadian speaking kingdom of
       <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">
        Assyria
       </a>
       had risen to dominance in northern Iraq. Assyria expanded territorially into the north eastern Levant, central Iraq, and eastern Anatolia, forming the
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Assyrian_Empire" title="Old Assyrian Empire">
        Old Assyrian Empire
       </a>
       (circa 2035–1750 BC) under kings such as
       <a href="/wiki/Puzur-Ashur_I" title="Puzur-Ashur I">
        Puzur-Ashur I
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sargon_I" title="Sargon I">
        Sargon I
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ilushuma" title="Ilushuma">
        Ilushuma
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Erishum_I" title="Erishum I">
        Erishum I
       </a>
       , the latter of whom produced the most detailed set of law yet written
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       . The south broke up into a number of Akkadian speaking states,
       <a href="/wiki/Isin" title="Isin">
        Isin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Larsa" title="Larsa">
        Larsa
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Eshnunna" title="Eshnunna">
        Eshnunna
       </a>
       being the major ones.
      </p>
      <p>
       During the 20th century BC, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canaanite_language" title="Canaanite language">
        Canaanite
       </a>
       speaking
       <a href="/wiki/Amorites" title="Amorites">
        Amorites
       </a>
       began to migrate into southern Mesopotamia. Eventually, they began to set up small petty kingdoms in the south, as well as usurping the thrones of extant city states such as
       <a href="/wiki/Isin" title="Isin">
        Isin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Larsa" title="Larsa">
        Larsa
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Eshnunna" title="Eshnunna">
        Eshnunna
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:F0182_Louvre_Code_Hammourabi_Bas-relief_Sb8_rwk.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3500" data-file-width="3170" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/F0182_Louvre_Code_Hammourabi_Bas-relief_Sb8_rwk.jpg/220px-F0182_Louvre_Code_Hammourabi_Bas-relief_Sb8_rwk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/F0182_Louvre_Code_Hammourabi_Bas-relief_Sb8_rwk.jpg/330px-F0182_Louvre_Code_Hammourabi_Bas-relief_Sb8_rwk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/F0182_Louvre_Code_Hammourabi_Bas-relief_Sb8_rwk.jpg/440px-F0182_Louvre_Code_Hammourabi_Bas-relief_Sb8_rwk.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:F0182_Louvre_Code_Hammourabi_Bas-relief_Sb8_rwk.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Hammurabi" title="Hammurabi">
          Hammurabi
         </a>
         , depicted as receiving his royal insignia from
         <a href="/wiki/Shamash" title="Shamash">
          Shamash
         </a>
         . Relief on the upper part of the stele of
         <a href="/wiki/Code_of_Hammurabi" title="Code of Hammurabi">
          Hammurabi's code of laws
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       One of these small Amorite kingdoms founded in 1894 BC contained the then small administrative town of
       <a href="/wiki/Babylon" title="Babylon">
        Babylon
       </a>
       within its borders. It remained insignificant for over a century, overshadowed by older and more powerful states, such as Assyria, Elam, Isin, Ehnunna and Larsa.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1792 BC, an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amorite" title="Amorite">
        Amorite
       </a>
       ruler named
       <a href="/wiki/Hammurabi" title="Hammurabi">
        Hammurabi
       </a>
       came to power in this state, and immediately set about building Babylon from a minor town into a major city, declaring himself its king. Hammurabi conquered the whole of southern and central Iraq, as well as Elam to the east and Mari to the west, then engaged in a protracted war with the Assyrian king
       <a href="/wiki/Ishme-Dagan" title="Ishme-Dagan">
        Ishme-Dagan
       </a>
       for domination of the region, creating the short-lived
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Babylonian_Empire" title="Babylonian Empire">
        Babylonian Empire
       </a>
       . He eventually prevailed over the successor of Ishme-Dagan and subjected Assyria and its Anatolian colonies. By the middle of the eighteenth century BC, the Sumerians had lost their cultural identity and ceased to exist as a distinct people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Genetic and cultural analysis indicates that the
       <a href="/wiki/Marsh_Arabs" title="Marsh Arabs">
        Marsh Arabs
       </a>
       of southern Iraq are probably their most direct modern descendants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       It is from the period of Hammurabi that southern Iraq came to be known as
       <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">
        Babylonia
       </a>
       , while the north had already coalesced into
       <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">
        Assyria
       </a>
       hundreds of years before. However, his empire was short-lived, and rapidly collapsed after his death, with both Assyria and southern Iraq, in the form of the
       <a href="/wiki/Sealand_Dynasty" title="Sealand Dynasty">
        Sealand Dynasty
       </a>
       , falling back into native Akkadian hands. The foreign Amorites clung on to power in a once more weak and small Babylonia until it was sacked by the
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">
        Indo-European
       </a>
       speaking
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hittite_Empire" title="Hittite Empire">
        Hittite Empire
       </a>
       based in
       <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">
        Anatolia
       </a>
       in 1595 BC. After this, another foreign people, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Language_Isolate" title="Language Isolate">
        Language Isolate
       </a>
       speaking
       <a href="/wiki/Kassites" title="Kassites">
        Kassites
       </a>
       , originating in the
       <a href="/wiki/Zagros_Mountains" title="Zagros Mountains">
        Zagros Mountains
       </a>
       of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Iran" title="Ancient Iran">
        Ancient Iran
       </a>
       , seized control of Babylonia, where they were to rule for almost 600 years, by far the longest dynasty ever to rule in Babylon.
      </p>
      <p>
       Iraq was from this point divided into three polities:
       <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">
        Assyria
       </a>
       in the north,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kassite" title="Kassite">
        Kassite
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">
        Babylonia
       </a>
       in the south central region, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Sealand_Dynasty" title="Sealand Dynasty">
        Sealand Dynasty
       </a>
       in the far south. The Sealand Dynasty was finally conquered by Kassite Babylonia circa 1380 BC.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Assyrian_Empire" title="Middle Assyrian Empire">
        Middle Assyrian Empire
       </a>
       (1365–1020 BC) saw Assyria rise to be the most powerful nation in the known world. Beginning with the campaigns of
       <a href="/wiki/Ashur-uballit_I" title="Ashur-uballit I">
        Ashur-uballit I
       </a>
       , Assyria destroyed the rival
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurrian" title="Hurrian">
        Hurrian
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/Mitanni" title="Mitanni">
        Mitanni
       </a>
       Empire, annexed huge swathes of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hittite_Empire" title="Hittite Empire">
        Hittite Empire
       </a>
       for itself, annexed northern Babylonia from the Kassites, forced the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_Empire" title="Egyptian Empire">
        Egyptian Empire
       </a>
       from the region, and defeated the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elamites" title="Elamites">
        Elamites
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Phrygians" title="Phrygians">
        Phrygians
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canaanites" title="Canaanites">
        Canaanites
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phoenicians" title="Phoenicians">
        Phoenicians
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cilicians" title="Cilicians">
        Cilicians
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gutians" title="Gutians">
        Gutians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dilmun" title="Dilmun">
        Dilmunites
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Arameans" title="Arameans">
        Arameans
       </a>
       . At its height, the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Assyrian_Empire" title="Middle Assyrian Empire">
        Middle Assyrian Empire
       </a>
       stretched from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Caucasus" title="The Caucasus">
        The Caucasus
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Dilmun" title="Dilmun">
        Dilmun
       </a>
       (modern
       <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">
        Bahrain
       </a>
       ), and from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean" title="Mediterranean">
        Mediterranean
       </a>
       coasts of
       <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
        Phoenicia
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Zagros_Mountains" title="Zagros Mountains">
        Zagros Mountains
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">
        Iran
       </a>
       . In 1235 BC,
       <a href="/wiki/Tukulti-Ninurta_I" title="Tukulti-Ninurta I">
        Tukulti-Ninurta I
       </a>
       of Assyria took the throne of
       <a href="/wiki/Babylon" title="Babylon">
        Babylon
       </a>
       , thus becoming the very first
       <i>
        native Mesopotamian
       </i>
       to rule the state.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jehu-Obelisk-cropped.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="999" data-file-width="1557" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Jehu-Obelisk-cropped.jpg/220px-Jehu-Obelisk-cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Jehu-Obelisk-cropped.jpg/330px-Jehu-Obelisk-cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Jehu-Obelisk-cropped.jpg/440px-Jehu-Obelisk-cropped.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jehu-Obelisk-cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Jehu" title="Jehu">
          Jehu
         </a>
         , king of
         <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(Samaria)" title="Kingdom of Israel (Samaria)">
          Israel
         </a>
         , bows before Shalmaneser III of
         <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">
          Assyria
         </a>
         , 825 BC.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bronze_Age_collapse" title="Bronze Age collapse">
        Bronze Age collapse
       </a>
       (1200–900 BC), Babylonia was in a state of chaos, dominated for long periods by Assyria and
       <a href="/wiki/Elam" title="Elam">
        Elam
       </a>
       . The Kassites were driven from power by Assyria and Elam, allowing native south Mesopotamian kings to rule Babylonia for the first time, although often subject to Assyrian or Elamite rulers. However, these
       <a href="/wiki/East_Semitic_languages" title="East Semitic languages">
        East Semitic
       </a>
       Akkadian kings, were unable to prevent new waves of
       <a href="/wiki/West_Semitic_languages" title="West Semitic languages">
        West Semitic
       </a>
       migrants entering southern Iraq, and during the 11th century BC
       <a href="/wiki/Arameans" title="Arameans">
        Arameans
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Suteans" title="Suteans">
        Suteans
       </a>
       entered Babylonia from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Levant" title="The Levant">
        The Levant
       </a>
       , and these were followed in the late 10th to early 9th century BC by the migrant
       <a href="/wiki/Chaldea" title="Chaldea">
        Chaldeans
       </a>
       who were closely related to the earlier
       <a href="/wiki/Arameans" title="Arameans">
        Arameans
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Iron_Age">
        Iron Age
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       After a period of comparative decline in Assyria, it once more began to expand with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo_Assyrian_Empire" title="Neo Assyrian Empire">
        Neo Assyrian Empire
       </a>
       (935–605 BC). This was to be the largest empire the region had yet seen, and under rulers such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adad-Nirari_II" title="Adad-Nirari II">
        Adad-Nirari II
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ashurnasirpal_I" title="Ashurnasirpal I">
        Ashurnasirpal
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Shalmaneser_III" title="Shalmaneser III">
        Shalmaneser III
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Semiramis" title="Semiramis">
        Semiramis
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiglath-pileser_III" title="Tiglath-pileser III">
        Tiglath-pileser III
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sargon_II" title="Sargon II">
        Sargon II
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sennacherib" title="Sennacherib">
        Sennacherib
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Esarhaddon" title="Esarhaddon">
        Esarhaddon
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ashurbanipal" title="Ashurbanipal">
        Ashurbanipal
       </a>
       , Iraq became the centre of an empire stretching from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">
        Persia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Parthia" title="Parthia">
        Parthia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Elam" title="Elam">
        Elam
       </a>
       in the east, to
       <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">
        Cyprus
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Antioch" title="Antioch">
        Antioch
       </a>
       in the west, and from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Caucasus" title="The Caucasus">
        The Caucasus
       </a>
       in the north to
       <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
        Egypt
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nubia" title="Nubia">
        Nubia
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabia" title="Arabia">
        Arabia
       </a>
       in the south.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_people" title="Arab people">
        Arabs
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Chaldea" title="Chaldea">
        Chaldeans
       </a>
       are first mentioned in written history (circa 850 BC) in the annals of
       <a href="/wiki/Shalmaneser_III" title="Shalmaneser III">
        Shalmaneser III
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       It was during this period that an Akkadian influenced form of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Aramaic" title="Eastern Aramaic">
        Eastern Aramaic
       </a>
       was adopted by the Assyrians as the
       <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">
        lingua franca
       </a>
       of their vast empire, and Mesopotamian Aramaic began to supplant Akkadian as the spoken language of the general populace of both Assyria and Babylonia. The descendant dialects of this tongue survive amongst the
       <a href="/wiki/Mandaeans" title="Mandaeans">
        Mandaeans
       </a>
       of southern Iraq and
       <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">
        Assyrians
       </a>
       of northern Iraq to this day.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loewenjagd_-645-635_Niniveh.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Loewenjagd_-645-635_Niniveh.JPG/220px-Loewenjagd_-645-635_Niniveh.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Loewenjagd_-645-635_Niniveh.JPG/330px-Loewenjagd_-645-635_Niniveh.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Loewenjagd_-645-635_Niniveh.JPG/440px-Loewenjagd_-645-635_Niniveh.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Loewenjagd_-645-635_Niniveh.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Relief showing a
         <a href="/wiki/Lion_hunting" title="Lion hunting">
          lion hunt
         </a>
         , from the north palace of
         <a href="/wiki/Nineveh" title="Nineveh">
          Nineveh
         </a>
         , 645–635 BC.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the late 7th century BC, the Assyrian Empire tore itself apart with a series of brutal civil wars, weakening itself to such a degree that a coalition of its former subjects; the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Babylonians" title="Babylonians">
        Babylonians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chaldea" title="Chaldea">
        Chaldeans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">
        Medes
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">
        Persians
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parthians" title="Parthians">
        Parthians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">
        Scythians
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cimmerians" title="Cimmerians">
        Cimmerians
       </a>
       , were able to attack Assyria, finally bringing its empire down by 605 BC.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Babylonian_and_Persian_periods">
        Babylonian and Persian periods
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The short-lived
       <a href="/wiki/Neo-Babylonian_Empire" title="Neo-Babylonian Empire">
        Neo-Babylonian Empire
       </a>
       (620–539 BC) succeeded that of Assyria. It failed to attain the size, power or longevity of its predecessor; however, it came to dominate
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Levant" title="The Levant">
        The Levant
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">
        Canaan
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabia" title="Arabia">
        Arabia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(Samaria)" title="Kingdom of Israel (Samaria)">
        Israel
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Judah" title="Kingdom of Judah">
        Judah
       </a>
       , and to defeat
       <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
        Egypt
       </a>
       . Initially, Babylon was ruled by yet another foreign dynasty, that of the
       <a href="/wiki/Chaldea" title="Chaldea">
        Chaldeans
       </a>
       , who had migrated to the region in the late 10th or early 9th century BC. Its greatest king,
       <a href="/wiki/Nebuchadnezzar_II" title="Nebuchadnezzar II">
        Nebuchadnezzar II
       </a>
       , rivalled another non native ruler, the ethnically unrelated
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amorite" title="Amorite">
        Amorite
       </a>
       king
       <a href="/wiki/Hammurabi" title="Hammurabi">
        Hammurabi
       </a>
       , as the greatest king of Babylon. However, by 556 BC, the Chaldeans had been deposed from power by the Assyrian born
       <a href="/wiki/Nabonidus" title="Nabonidus">
        Nabonidus
       </a>
       and his son and regent
       <a href="/wiki/Belshazzar" title="Belshazzar">
        Belshazzar
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 6th century BC,
       <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_the_Great" title="Cyrus the Great">
        Cyrus the Great
       </a>
       of neighbouring
       <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">
        Persia
       </a>
       defeated the
       <a href="/wiki/Neo-Babylonian_Empire" title="Neo-Babylonian Empire">
        Neo-Babylonian Empire
       </a>
       at the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Opis" title="Battle of Opis">
        Battle of Opis
       </a>
       and Iraq was subsumed into the
       <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">
        Achaemenid Empire
       </a>
       for nearly two centuries. The Achaemenids made
       <a href="/wiki/Babylon" title="Babylon">
        Babylon
       </a>
       their main capital. The Chaldeans and Chaldea disappeared at around this time, though both Assyria and Babylonia endured and thrived under Achaemenid rule (see
       <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Assyria" title="Achaemenid Assyria">
        Achaemenid Assyria
       </a>
       ). Little changed under the Persians, having spent three centuries under Assyrian rule, their kings saw themselves as successors to Ashurbanipal, and they retained Assyrian Imperial Aramaic as the language of empire, together with the Assyrian imperial infrastructure, and an Assyrian style of art and architecture.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diadochen1.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="961" data-file-width="2000" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Diadochen1.png/220px-Diadochen1.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Diadochen1.png/330px-Diadochen1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Diadochen1.png/440px-Diadochen1.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Diadochen1.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Greek-ruled
         <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">
          Seleucid Empire
         </a>
         (in yellow) with capital in
         <a href="/wiki/Seleucia" title="Seleucia">
          Seleucia
         </a>
         on the Tigris, north of Babylon.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the late 4th century BC,
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">
        Alexander the Great
       </a>
       conquered the region, putting it under
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hellenistic_civilization" title="Hellenistic civilization">
        Hellenistic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">
        Seleucid
       </a>
       rule for over two centuries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Seleucids introduced the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indo-Anatolian" title="Indo-Anatolian">
        Indo-Anatolian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">
        Greek
       </a>
       term
       <i>
        Syria
       </i>
       to the region. This name had for many centuries been the Indo-European word for
       <i>
        Assyria
       </i>
       and specifically and only meant Assyria; however, the Seleucids also applied it to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Levant" title="The Levant">
        The Levant
       </a>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aramea" title="Aramea">
        Aramea
       </a>
       , causing both the Assyria and the Assyrians of Iraq and the
       <a href="/wiki/Arameans" title="Arameans">
        Arameans
       </a>
       and The Levant to be called Syria and Syrians/Syriacs in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greco-Roman" title="Greco-Roman">
        Greco-Roman
       </a>
       world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hatra_ruins.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="396" data-file-width="600" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Hatra_ruins.jpg/220px-Hatra_ruins.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Hatra_ruins.jpg/330px-Hatra_ruins.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Hatra_ruins.jpg/440px-Hatra_ruins.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hatra_ruins.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Flourished in the 2nd century, the strongly fortified Parthian city of
         <a href="/wiki/Hatra" title="Hatra">
          Hatra
         </a>
         shows a unique blend of both
         <a href="/wiki/Classical_architecture" title="Classical architecture">
          Classical
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Iranian_architecture" title="Iranian architecture">
          Persian
         </a>
         architecture and art.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
          <a href="#cite_note-33">
           [33]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
          <a href="#cite_note-34">
           [34]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">
        Parthians
       </a>
       (247 BC – 224 AD) from Persia conquered the region during the reign of
       <a href="/wiki/Mithridates_I_of_Parthia" title="Mithridates I of Parthia">
        Mithridates I of Parthia
       </a>
       (r. 171–138 BC). From
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syria_(Roman_province)" title="Syria (Roman province)">
        Syria
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Romans
       </a>
       invaded western parts of the region
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman-Parthian_Wars" title="Roman-Parthian Wars">
        several times
       </a>
       , briefly founding
       <i>
        Assyria Provincia
       </i>
       in Assyria.
       <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
        Christianity
       </a>
       began to take hold in Iraq (particularly in
       <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">
        Assyria
       </a>
       ) between the 1st and 3rd centuries, and Assyria became a centre of
       <a href="/wiki/Syriac_Christianity" title="Syriac Christianity">
        Syriac Christianity
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_East" title="Church of the East">
        Church of the East
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Syriac_literature" title="Syriac literature">
        Syriac literature
       </a>
       . A number of indigenous independent
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-Assyrian" title="Neo-Assyrian">
        Neo-Assyrian
       </a>
       states evolved in the north during the Parthian era, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Adiabene" title="Adiabene">
        Adiabene
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Assur" title="Assur">
        Assur
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Osroene" title="Osroene">
        Osroene
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Hatra" title="Hatra">
        Hatra
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanid_dynasty" title="Sassanid dynasty">
        Sassanids
       </a>
       of Persia under
       <a href="/wiki/Ardashir_I" title="Ardashir I">
        Ardashir I
       </a>
       destroyed the Parthian Empire and conquered the region in 224 AD. During the 240s and 250's AD, the Sassanids gradually conquered the small Neo Assyrian states, culminating with Assur in 256 AD. The region was thus a province of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanid_Empire" title="Sassanid Empire">
        Sassanid Empire
       </a>
       for over four centuries (see also;
       <a href="/wiki/As%C5%8Drist%C4%81n" title="Asōristān">
        Asōristān
       </a>
       ), and became the frontier and battle ground between the Sassanid Empire and
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
        Byzantine Empire
       </a>
       , with both empires weakening each other, paving the way for the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">
        Arab
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Persia" title="Muslim conquest of Persia">
        Muslim conquest of Persia
       </a>
       in the mid-7th century.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Abbasids850.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="902" data-file-width="1481" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Abbasids850.png/300px-Abbasids850.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Abbasids850.png/450px-Abbasids850.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Abbasids850.png/600px-Abbasids850.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Abbasids850.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">
          Abbasid Caliphate
         </a>
