         at its greatest extent, c. 850.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Arab Islamic conquest in the mid-7th century AD established
       <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
        Islam
       </a>
       in Iraq and saw a large influx of
       <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">
        Arabs
       </a>
       . Under the
       <a href="/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate" title="Rashidun Caliphate">
        Rashidun Caliphate
       </a>
       , the prophet
       <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">
        Muhammad
       </a>
       's cousin and son-in-law,
       <a href="/wiki/Ali" title="Ali">
        Ali
       </a>
       , moved his capital to
       <a href="/wiki/Kufa" title="Kufa">
        Kufa
       </a>
       when he became the fourth
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caliph" title="Caliph">
        caliph
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">
        Umayyad Caliphate
       </a>
       ruled the province of Iraq from
       <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">
        Damascus
       </a>
       in the 7th century. (However, eventually there was a separate, independent
       <a href="/wiki/Caliphate_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Caliphate of Córdoba">
        Caliphate of Córdoba
       </a>
       in Iberia.)
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">
        Abbasid Caliphate
       </a>
       built the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">
        Baghdad
       </a>
       in the 8th century as its capital, and the city became the leading metropolis of the
       <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">
        Arab
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">
        Muslim world
       </a>
       for five centuries. Baghdad was the largest
       <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">
        multicultural
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">
        city
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </a>
       , peaking at a population of more than a million,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and was the centre of learning during the
       <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">
        Islamic Golden Age
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">
        Mongols
       </a>
       destroyed the city and burned its library during the
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Baghdad_(1258)" title="Siege of Baghdad (1258)">
        siege of Baghdad
       </a>
       in the 13th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1257,
       <a href="/wiki/Hulagu_Khan" title="Hulagu Khan">
        Hulagu Khan
       </a>
       amassed an unusually large army, a significant portion of the Mongol Empire's forces, for the purpose of conquering Baghdad. When they arrived at the Islamic capital, Hulagu Khan demanded its surrender, but the last Abbasid Caliph
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Musta%27sim" title="Al-Musta'sim">
        Al-Musta'sim
       </a>
       refused. This angered Hulagu, and, consistent with Mongol strategy of discouraging resistance, he
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Baghdad_(1258)" title="Siege of Baghdad (1258)">
        besieged Baghdad
       </a>
       , sacked the city and massacred many of the inhabitants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Estimates of the number of dead range from 200,000 to a million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bagdad1258.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1464" data-file-width="2074" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Bagdad1258.jpg/220px-Bagdad1258.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Bagdad1258.jpg/330px-Bagdad1258.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Bagdad1258.jpg/440px-Bagdad1258.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bagdad1258.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Baghdad_(1258)" title="Siege of Baghdad (1258)">
          sack of Baghdad
         </a>
         by the Mongols.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Mongols destroyed the Abbasid Caliphate and Baghdad's
       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Wisdom" title="House of Wisdom">
        House of Wisdom
       </a>
       , which contained countless precious and historical documents. The city has never regained its previous pre-eminence as a major centre of culture and influence. Some historians believe that the Mongol invasion destroyed much of the
       <a href="/wiki/Irrigation" title="Irrigation">
        irrigation
       </a>
       infrastructure that had sustained Mesopotamia for millennia. Other historians point to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soil_salination" title="Soil salination">
        soil salination
       </a>
       as the culprit in the decline in agriculture.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The mid-14th-century
       <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">
        Black Death
       </a>
       ravaged much of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_world" title="Islamic world">
        Islamic world
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The best estimate for the Middle East is a death rate of roughly one-third.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1401, a warlord of Mongol descent,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tamerlane" title="Tamerlane">
        Tamerlane
       </a>
       (Timur Lenk), invaded Iraq. After the capture of Baghdad, 20,000 of its citizens were massacred.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Timur ordered that every soldier should return with at least two severed human heads to show him (many warriors were so scared they killed prisoners captured earlier in the campaign just to ensure they had heads to present to Timur).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Timur also conducted massacres of the indigenous
       <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">
        Assyrian
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">
        Christian
       </a>
       population, hitherto still the majority population in northern Mesopotamia, and it was during this time that the ancient Assyrian city of
       <a href="/wiki/Assur" title="Assur">
        Assur
       </a>
       was finally abandoned.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_Iraq">
        Ottoman Iraq
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Iraq" title="Ottoman Iraq">
        Ottoman Iraq
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mamluk_dynasty_of_Iraq" title="Mamluk dynasty of Iraq">
        Mamluk dynasty of Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cedid_Atlas_(Middle_East)_1803.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="8199" data-file-width="10840" height="265" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Cedid_Atlas_%28Middle_East%29_1803.jpg/350px-Cedid_Atlas_%28Middle_East%29_1803.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Cedid_Atlas_%28Middle_East%29_1803.jpg/525px-Cedid_Atlas_%28Middle_East%29_1803.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Cedid_Atlas_%28Middle_East%29_1803.jpg/700px-Cedid_Atlas_%28Middle_East%29_1803.jpg 2x" width="350"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cedid_Atlas_(Middle_East)_1803.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The 1803
         <a href="/wiki/Cedid_Atlas" title="Cedid Atlas">
          Cedid Atlas
         </a>
         , showing the area today known as Iraq divided between "
         <a href="/wiki/Upper_Mesopotamia" title="Upper Mesopotamia">
          Al Jazira
         </a>
         " (pink), "
         <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan" title="Kurdistan">
          Kurdistan
         </a>
         " (blue), "Iraq" (green), and "
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al_Sham" title="Al Sham">
          Al Sham
         </a>
         " (yellow).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the late 14th and early 15th centuries, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Sheep_Turkmen" title="Black Sheep Turkmen">
        Black Sheep Turkmen
       </a>
       ruled the area now known as Iraq. In 1466, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Sheep_Turkmen" title="White Sheep Turkmen">
        White Sheep Turkmen
       </a>
       defeated the Black Sheep and took control. From the earliest 16th century, in 1508, as with all territories of the former White Sheep Turkmen, Iraq fell into the hands of the Iranian
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Safavids" title="Safavids">
        Safavids
       </a>
       . Owing to the century long Turco-Iranian rivalry between the Safavids and the neighbouring
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turks" title="Ottoman Turks">
        Ottoman Turks
       </a>
       , Iraq would be contested between the two for more than a hundred years during the frequent
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman-Persian_Wars" title="Ottoman-Persian Wars">
        Ottoman-Persian Wars
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       With the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Zuhab" title="Treaty of Zuhab">
        Treaty of Zuhab
       </a>
       in 1639, most of the territory of present-day Iraq eventually came under the control of Ottoman Empire as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eyalet_of_Baghdad" title="Eyalet of Baghdad">
        eyalet of Baghdad
       </a>
       as a result of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman-Persian_Wars" title="Ottoman-Persian Wars">
        wars
       </a>
       with the neighbouring rival,
       <a href="/wiki/Safavid_dynasty" title="Safavid dynasty">
        Safavid Iran
       </a>
       . Throughout most of the period of Ottoman rule (1533–1918), the territory of present-day Iraq was a battle zone between the rival regional empires and tribal alliances.
      </p>
      <p>
       By the 17th century, the frequent conflicts with the Safavids had sapped the strength of the Ottoman Empire and had weakened its control over its provinces. The nomadic population swelled with the influx of
       <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">
        bedouins
       </a>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/Najd" title="Najd">
        Najd
       </a>
       , in the Arabian Peninsula. Bedouin raids on settled areas became impossible to curb.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Layard_Nineveh.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="598" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Layard_Nineveh.jpg/220px-Layard_Nineveh.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Layard_Nineveh.jpg/330px-Layard_Nineveh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Layard_Nineveh.jpg/440px-Layard_Nineveh.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Layard_Nineveh.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         English archaeologist
         <a href="/wiki/Austen_Henry_Layard" title="Austen Henry Layard">
          Austen Henry Layard
         </a>
         in the ancient
         <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">
          Assyrian
         </a>
         city of
         <a href="/wiki/Nineveh" title="Nineveh">
          Nineveh
         </a>
         , 1852.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the years 1747–1831, Iraq was ruled by a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mamluk_dynasty_of_Iraq" title="Mamluk dynasty of Iraq">
        Mamluk dynasty
       </a>
       of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georgian_people" title="Georgian people">
        Georgian
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbs_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-bbs-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       origin who succeeded in obtaining autonomy from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman_Porte" title="Ottoman Porte">
        Ottoman Porte
       </a>
       , suppressed tribal revolts, curbed the power of the Janissaries, restored order and introduced a programme of modernisation of economy and military. In 1831, the Ottomans managed to overthrow the Mamluk regime and imposed their direct control over Iraq. The population of Iraq, estimated at 30 million in 800 AD, was only 5 million at the start of the 20th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       , the Ottomans sided with
       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
        Germany
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">
        Central Powers
       </a>
       . In the
       <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamian_campaign" title="Mesopotamian campaign">
        Mesopotamian campaign
       </a>
       against the Central Powers,
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
        British
       </a>
       forces invaded the country and initially suffered a major defeat at the hands of the Turkish army during the
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Kut" title="Siege of Kut">
        Siege of Kut
       </a>
       (1915–1916). However, subsequent to this the British began to gain the upper hand, and were further aided by the support of local
       <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">
        Arabs
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrians_in_Iraq" title="Assyrians in Iraq">
        Assyrians
       </a>
       . In 1916, the British and French made a plan for the post-war division of
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">
        Western Asia
       </a>
       under the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sykes-Picot_Agreement" title="Sykes-Picot Agreement">
        Sykes-Picot Agreement
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       British forces regrouped and
       <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Baghdad_(1917)" title="Fall of Baghdad (1917)">
        captured Baghdad
       </a>
       in 1917, and defeated the Ottomans. An armistice was signed in 1918.
      </p>
      <p>
       During World War I, the Ottomans were defeated and driven from much of the area by the United Kingdom during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Dissolution of the Ottoman Empire">
        dissolution of the Ottoman Empire
       </a>
       . The British lost 92,000 soldiers in the Mesopotamian campaign. Ottoman losses are unknown but the British captured a total of 45,000
       <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_war" title="Prisoner of war">
        prisoners of war
       </a>
       . By the end of 1918, the British had deployed 410,000 men in the area, of which 112,000 were combat troops.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="British_administration_and_independent_Kingdom">
        British administration and independent Kingdom
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Iraq" title="Mandatory Iraq">
        Mandatory Iraq
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Iraq" title="Kingdom of Iraq">
        Kingdom of Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BritsLookingOnBaghdad1941.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="798" data-file-width="800" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/BritsLookingOnBaghdad1941.jpg/220px-BritsLookingOnBaghdad1941.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/BritsLookingOnBaghdad1941.jpg/330px-BritsLookingOnBaghdad1941.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/BritsLookingOnBaghdad1941.jpg/440px-BritsLookingOnBaghdad1941.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BritsLookingOnBaghdad1941.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         British troops in Baghdad, June 1941.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On 11 November 1920, Iraq became a
       <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">
        League of Nations mandate
       </a>
       under British control with the name "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Mandate_of_Mesopotamia" title="British Mandate of Mesopotamia">
        State of Iraq
       </a>
       ". The British established the
       <a href="/wiki/Hashemites" title="Hashemites">
        Hashemite
       </a>
       king,
       <a href="/wiki/Faisal_I_of_Iraq" title="Faisal I of Iraq">
        Faisal I of Iraq
       </a>
       , who had been forced out of
       <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
        Syria
       </a>
       by the French, as their client ruler. Likewise, British authorities selected
       <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">
        Sunni
       </a>
       Arab elites from the region for appointments to government and ministry offices.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
          <span title="Statement needs to be more specific about the content to which it refers. (April 2007)">
           specify
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
          <span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (February 2013)">
           page needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Faced with spiraling costs and influenced by the public protestations of the war hero
       <a href="/wiki/T._E._Lawrence" title="T. E. Lawrence">
        T. E. Lawrence
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">
         The Times
        </a>
       </i>
       , Britain replaced
       <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Wilson" title="Arnold Wilson">
        Arnold Wilson
       </a>
       in October 1920 with a new Civil Commissioner,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Percy_Zachariah_Cox" title="Percy Zachariah Cox">
        Sir Percy Cox
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cox managed to quell a rebellion, yet was also responsible for implementing the fateful policy of close co-operation with Iraq's Sunni minority.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The institution of
       <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">
        slavery
       </a>
       was abolished in the 1920s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zanj_53-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-zanj-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Britain granted independence to the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Iraq" title="Kingdom of Iraq">
        Kingdom of Iraq
       </a>
       in 1932,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       on the urging of
       <a href="/wiki/Faisal_I_of_Iraq" title="Faisal I of Iraq">
        King Faisal
       </a>
       , though the British retained
       <a href="/wiki/Military_base" title="Military base">
        military bases
       </a>
       , local militia in the form of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrian_Levies" title="Assyrian Levies">
        Assyrian Levies
       </a>
       , and transit rights for their forces. King
       <a href="/wiki/Ghazi_of_Iraq" title="Ghazi of Iraq">
        Ghazi
       </a>
       ruled as a figurehead after King Faisal's death in 1933, while undermined by attempted military
       <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">
        coups
       </a>
       , until his death in 1939. Ghazi was followed by his underage son,
       <a href="/wiki/Faisal_II_of_Iraq" title="Faisal II of Iraq">
        Faisal II
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/%27Abd_al-Ilah" title="'Abd al-Ilah">
        'Abd al-Ilah
       </a>
       served as
       <a href="/wiki/Regent" title="Regent">
        Regent
       </a>
       during Faisal's minority.
      </p>
      <p>
       On 1 April 1941,
       <a href="/wiki/Rashid_Ali_al-Gaylani" title="Rashid Ali al-Gaylani">
        Rashid Ali al-Gaylani
       </a>
       and members of the
       <a href="/wiki/Golden_Square_(Iraq)" title="Golden Square (Iraq)">
        Golden Square
       </a>
       staged a
       <a href="/wiki/1941_Iraqi_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1941 Iraqi coup d'état">
        coup d'état and overthrew the government of 'Abd al-Ilah
       </a>
       . During the subsequent
       <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Iraqi_War" title="Anglo-Iraqi War">
        Anglo-Iraqi War
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
        United Kingdom
       </a>
       (which still maintained air bases in Iraq) invaded Iraq for fear that the Rashid Ali government might cut oil supplies to Western nations because of his links to the
       <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">
        Axis powers
       </a>
       . The war started on 2 May, and the British, together with loyal
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrian_Levies" title="Assyrian Levies">
        Assyrian Levies
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       defeated the forces of Al-Gaylani, forcing an armistice on 31 May.
      </p>
      <p>
       A
       <a href="/wiki/Military_occupation" title="Military occupation">
        military occupation
       </a>
       followed the restoration of the pre-coup government of the
       <a href="/wiki/Hashemites" title="Hashemites">
        Hashemite
       </a>
       monarchy. The occupation ended on 26 October 1947, although Britain was to retain military bases in Iraq until 1954, after which the Assyrian militias were disbanded. The rulers during the occupation and the remainder of the Hashemite monarchy were
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuri_as-Said" title="Nuri as-Said">
        Nuri as-Said
       </a>
       , the autocratic Prime Minister, who also ruled from 1930 to 1932, and 'Abd al-Ilah, the former Regent who now served as an adviser to King Faisal II.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Republic_and_Ba.27athist_Iraq">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_and_Ba'athist_Iraq">
        Republic and Ba'athist Iraq
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Republic_(1958%E2%80%9368)" title="Iraqi Republic (1958–68)">
        Iraqi Republic (1958–68)
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ba%27athist_Iraq" title="Ba'athist Iraq">
        Ba'athist Iraq
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War" title="Iran–Iraq War">
        Iran–Iraq War
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1958_revolution_in_Iraq.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="411" data-file-width="531" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/1958_revolution_in_Iraq.jpg/220px-1958_revolution_in_Iraq.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/1958_revolution_in_Iraq.jpg/330px-1958_revolution_in_Iraq.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/1958_revolution_in_Iraq.jpg/440px-1958_revolution_in_Iraq.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1958_revolution_in_Iraq.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/14_July_Revolution" title="14 July Revolution">
          14 July Revolution
         </a>
         in 1958.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1958, a coup d'état known as the
       <a href="/wiki/14_July_Revolution" title="14 July Revolution">
        14 July Revolution
       </a>
       was led by the Brigadier General
       <a href="/wiki/Abd_al-Karim_Qasim" title="Abd al-Karim Qasim">
        Abd al-Karim Qasim
       </a>
       . This revolt was strongly anti-imperial and anti-monarchical in nature and had strong socialist elements. Numerous people were killed in the coup, including King
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faysal_II" title="Faysal II">
        Faysal II
       </a>
       , Prince
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abd_al-Ilah" title="Abd al-Ilah">
        Abd al-Ilah
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuri_al-Sa%27id" title="Nuri al-Sa'id">
        Nuri al-Sa'id
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Qasim controlled Iraq through military rule and in 1958 he began a process of forcibly reducing the surplus amounts of land owned by a few citizens and having the state redistribute the land. He was overthrown by Colonel
       <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Salam_Arif" title="Abdul Salam Arif">
        Abdul Salam Arif
       </a>
       in a
       <a href="/wiki/Ramadan_Revolution" title="Ramadan Revolution">
        February 1963 coup
       </a>
       . After the latter's death in 1966, he was succeeded by his brother,
       <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Rahman_Arif" title="Abdul Rahman Arif">
        Abdul Rahman Arif
       </a>
       , who was
       <a href="/wiki/17_July_Revolution" title="17 July Revolution">
        overthrown
       </a>
       by the
       <a href="/wiki/Arab_Socialist_Ba%27ath_Party_%E2%80%93_Iraq_Region" title="Arab Socialist Ba'ath Party – Iraq Region">
        Ba'ath Party
       </a>
       in 1968.
       <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Hassan_al-Bakr" title="Ahmed Hassan al-Bakr">
        Ahmed Hassan al-Bakr
       </a>
       became the first Ba'ath
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_Iraq" title="President of Iraq">
        President of Iraq
       </a>
       but then the movement gradually came under the control of
       <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">
        Saddam Hussein
       </a>
       , who acceded to the presidency and control of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_Revolutionary_Command_Council" title="Iraqi Revolutionary Command Council">
        Revolutionary Command Council
       </a>
       (RCC), then Iraq's supreme executive body, in July 1979.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1979, the
       <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Revolution" title="Iranian Revolution">
        Iranian Revolution
       </a>
       took place. Following months of cross-border raids between the two countries, Saddam declared war on Iran in September 1980, initiating the
       <a href="/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War" title="Iran–Iraq War">
        Iran–Iraq War
       </a>
       (or First Persian Gulf War). Taking advantage of the post-revolution chaos in Iran, Iraq captured some territories in southwest of Iran, but Iran recaptured all of the lost territories within two years, and for the next six years Iran was on the offensive.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
          <span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2014)">
           page needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The war, which ended in
       <a href="/wiki/Stalemate" title="Stalemate">
        stalemate
       </a>
       in 1988, had cost the lives of between half a million and 1.5 million people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1981, Israeli aircraft
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Opera" title="Operation Opera">
        bombed an Iraqi nuclear materials testing reactor at Osirak
       </a>
       and was widely criticised at the United Nations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During the 8-year war with Iran, Saddam Hussein extensively used
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_chemical_weapons_program" title="Iraqi chemical weapons program">
        chemical weapons
       </a>
       against Iranians.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the final stages of the Iran–Iraq War, the Ba'athist Iraqi regime led the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Anfal_Campaign" title="Al-Anfal Campaign">
        Al-Anfal Campaign
       </a>
       , a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genocidal" title="Genocidal">
        genocidal
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrw.org_62-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-hrw.org-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       campaign that targeted Iraqi Kurds,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and led to the killing of 50,000–100,000 civilians.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Chemical weapons were also used against
       <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam_in_Iraq" title="Shia Islam in Iraq">
        Iraqi Shia
       </a>
       civilians during the
       <a href="/wiki/1991_uprisings_in_Iraq" title="1991 uprisings in Iraq">
        1991 uprisings in Iraq
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In August 1990,
       <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Kuwait" title="Invasion of Kuwait">
        Iraq invaded and annexed Kuwait
       </a>
       . This subsequently led to
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">
        military intervention
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       -led forces in the First
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">
        Gulf War
       </a>
       . The coalition forces proceeded with a bombing campaign targeting military targets
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crusade_67-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Crusade-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arbuthnot_68-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Arbuthnot-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSM2002_69-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CSM2002-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and then launched a 100-hour-long ground assault against Iraqi forces in Southern Iraq and those occupying Kuwait.
      </p>
      <p>
       Iraq's armed forces were devastated during the war. Shortly after it ended in 1991, Shia and
       <a href="/wiki/Kurds_in_Iraq" title="Kurds in Iraq">
        Kurdish Iraqis
       </a>
       led
       <a href="/wiki/1991_uprisings_in_Iraq" title="1991 uprisings in Iraq">
        several uprisings
       </a>
       against Saddam Hussein's regime, but these were successfully repressed using the Iraqi security forces and chemical weapons. It is estimated that as many as 100,000 people, including many civilians were killed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During the uprisings the US, UK, France and Turkey, claiming authority under
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_688" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 688">
        UNSCR 688
       </a>
       , established the
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_no-fly_zones" title="Iraqi no-fly zones">
        Iraqi no-fly zones
       </a>
       to protect Kurdish and Shiite populations from attacks by the Saddam regime's fixed-wing aircraft (but not helicopters).
      </p>
      <p>
       Iraq was ordered to destroy its chemical and biological weapons and the UN attempted to compel Saddam's government to disarm and agree to a ceasefire by imposing additional sanctions on the country in addition to the initial sanctions imposed following Iraq's invasion of Kuwait. The Iraqi Government's failure to disarm and agree to a ceasefire resulted in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraq_sanctions" title="Iraq sanctions">
        sanctions
       </a>
       which remained in place until 2003. The effects of the sanctions on the civilian population of Iraq have been disputed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unicef99_71-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-unicef99-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rubin_72-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Rubin-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Whereas it was widely believed that the sanctions caused a major rise in child mortality, recent research has shown that commonly cited data were fabricated by the Iraqi government and that "there was no major rise in child mortality in Iraq after 1990 and during the period of the sanctions."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spagat_73-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Spagat-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_74-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       An
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_for_food_program" title="Oil for food program">
        oil for food program
       </a>
       was established in 1996 to ease the effects of sanctions.
      </p>
      <p>
       Following the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/9/11_terrorist_attacks" title="9/11 terrorist attacks">
        9/11 terrorist attacks
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_George_W._Bush" title="Presidency of George W. Bush">
        George W. Bush administration
       </a>
       began planning the overthrow of Saddam's government and in October 2002, the US Congress passed the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joint_Resolution_to_Authorize_the_Use_of_United_States_Armed_Forces_Against_Iraq" title="Joint Resolution to Authorize the Use of United States Armed Forces Against Iraq">
        Joint Resolution to Authorize the Use of United States Armed Forces Against Iraq
       </a>
       . In November 2002, the UN Security Council passed
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1441" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1441">
        UNSCR 1441
       </a>
       and in March 2003 the US and its allies invaded Iraq.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="2003.E2.80.932007">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="2003–2007">
        2003–2007
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SaddamStatue.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="303" data-file-width="252" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/SaddamStatue.jpg/170px-SaddamStatue.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c1/SaddamStatue.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SaddamStatue.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The April 2003 toppling of
         <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">
          Saddam Hussein
         </a>
         's statue in
         <a href="/wiki/Firdos_Square" title="Firdos Square">
          Firdos Square
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">
          Baghdad
         </a>
         shortly after the
         <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">
          Iraq War
         </a>
         invasion.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">
        2003 invasion of Iraq
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Iraq_(2003%E2%80%9311)" title="History of Iraq (2003–11)">
        History of Iraq (2003–11)
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">
        Iraq War
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       On 20 March 2003, a United States-organized coalition
       <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">
        invaded Iraq
       </a>
       , under the pretext that Iraq had failed to abandon its
       <a href="/wiki/Iraq_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="Iraq and weapons of mass destruction">
        weapons of mass destruction program
       </a>
       in violation of
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_687" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 687">
        UN Resolution 687
       </a>
       . This claim was based on documents provided by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIA" title="CIA">
        CIA
       </a>
       and the British government
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and were later
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duelfer_Report" title="Duelfer Report">
        found to be unreliable
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Following the invasion, the United States established the
       <a href="/wiki/Coalition_Provisional_Authority" title="Coalition Provisional Authority">
        Coalition Provisional Authority
       </a>
       to govern Iraq. In May 2003
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L._Paul_Bremer" title="L. Paul Bremer">
        L. Paul Bremer
       </a>
       , the chief executive of the CPA, issued orders to
       <a href="/wiki/De-Ba%27athification" title="De-Ba'athification">
        exclude Baath Party members
       </a>
       from the new Iraqi government (CPA Order 1) and to disband the Iraqi Army (
       <a href="/wiki/Coalition_Provisional_Authority_Order_2" title="Coalition Provisional Authority Order 2">
        CPA Order 2
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The decision dissolved the largely Sunni Iraqi Army
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and excluded many of the country's former government officials from participating in the country's governance, including 40,000 school teachers who had joined the Baath Party simply to keep their jobs,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       helping to bring about a chaotic post-invasion environment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_insurgency_(2003%E2%80%9306)" title="Iraqi insurgency (2003–06)">
        An insurgency
       </a>
       against the
       <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">
        US-led coalition
       </a>
       -rule of Iraq began in summer 2003 within elements of the former Iraqi secret police and army, who formed guerilla units. In fall 2003, self-entitled '
       <a href="/wiki/Jihad" title="Jihad">
        jihadist
       </a>
       ' groups began targeting coalition forces. Various Sunni militias were created in 2003, for example
       <a href="/wiki/Jama%27at_al-Tawhid_wal-Jihad" title="Jama'at al-Tawhid wal-Jihad">
        Jama'at al-Tawhid wal-Jihad
       </a>
       led by
       <a href="/wiki/Abu_Musab_al-Zarqawi" title="Abu Musab al-Zarqawi">
        Abu Musab al-Zarqawi
       </a>
       . The insurgency included intense inter-ethnic violence between Sunnis and Shias.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn.com_83-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cnn.com-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Abu_Ghraib_torture_and_prisoner_abuse" title="Abu Ghraib torture and prisoner abuse">
        Abu Ghraib torture and prisoner abuse
       </a>
       scandal came to light, late 2003 in reports by
       <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">
        Amnesty International
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">
        Associated Press
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_031016-N-3236B-043_A_marine_patrols_the_streets_of_Al_Faw,_Iraq.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1960" data-file-width="3008" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/US_Navy_031016-N-3236B-043_A_marine_patrols_the_streets_of_Al_Faw%2C_Iraq.jpg/220px-US_Navy_031016-N-3236B-043_A_marine_patrols_the_streets_of_Al_Faw%2C_Iraq.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/US_Navy_031016-N-3236B-043_A_marine_patrols_the_streets_of_Al_Faw%2C_Iraq.jpg/330px-US_Navy_031016-N-3236B-043_A_marine_patrols_the_streets_of_Al_Faw%2C_Iraq.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/US_Navy_031016-N-3236B-043_A_marine_patrols_the_streets_of_Al_Faw%2C_Iraq.jpg/440px-US_Navy_031016-N-3236B-043_A_marine_patrols_the_streets_of_Al_Faw%2C_Iraq.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_031016-N-3236B-043_A_marine_patrols_the_streets_of_Al_Faw,_Iraq.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">
          US Marines
         </a>
         patrol the streets of
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al_Faw" title="Al Faw">
          Al Faw
         </a>
         , October 2003.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahdi_Army" title="Mahdi Army">
        Mahdi Army
       </a>
       —a Shia militia created in the summer of 2003 by
       <a href="/wiki/Muqtada_al-Sadr" title="Muqtada al-Sadr">
        Muqtada al-Sadr
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mehdi_84-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mehdi-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       —began to fight Coalition forces in April 2004.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mehdi_84-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-mehdi-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       2004 saw Sunni and Shia militants fighting against each other and against the new
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Interim_Government" title="Iraqi Interim Government">
        Iraqi Interim Government
       </a>
       installed in June 2004, and against Coalition forces, as well as the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_Fallujah" title="First Battle of Fallujah">
        First Battle of Fallujah
       </a>
       in April and
       <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Fallujah" title="Second Battle of Fallujah">
        Second Battle of Fallujah
       </a>
       in November. The Sunni militia Jama'at al-Tawhid wal-Jihad became
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda_in_Iraq" title="Al-Qaeda in Iraq">
        Al-Qaeda in Iraq
       </a>
       in October 2004 and targeted Coalition forces as well as civilians, mainly Shia Muslims, further exacerbating ethnic tensions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In January 2005, the
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_parliamentary_election,_January_2005" title="Iraqi parliamentary election, January 2005">
        first elections
       </a>
       since the invasion took place and in October a
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Iraq" title="Constitution of Iraq">
        new Constitution
       </a>
       was approved, which was followed by
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_parliamentary_election,_December_2005" title="Iraqi parliamentary election, December 2005">
        parliamentary elections
       </a>
       in December. However, insurgent attacks were common and increased to 34,131 in 2005 from 26,496 in 2004.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During 2006, fighting continued and reached its highest levels of violence, more
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haditha_killings" title="Haditha killings">
        war crimes scandals
       </a>
       were made public,
       <a href="/wiki/Abu_Musab_al-Zarqawi" title="Abu Musab al-Zarqawi">
        Abu Musab al-Zarqawi
       </a>
       the leader of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda_in_Iraq" title="Al-Qaeda in Iraq">
        Al-Qaeda in Iraq
       </a>
       was killed by US forces and Iraq's former dictator
       <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">
        Saddam Hussein
       </a>
       was sentenced to death for
       <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">
        crimes against humanity
       </a>
       and hanged.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In late 2006, the US government's
       <a href="/wiki/Iraq_Study_Group" title="Iraq Study Group">
        Iraq Study Group
       </a>
       recommended that the US begin focusing on training Iraqi military personnel and in January 2007 US President George W. Bush announced a
       <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War_troop_surge_of_2007" title="Iraq War troop surge of 2007">
        "Surge"
       </a>
       in the number of US troops deployed to the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In May 2007, Iraq's Parliament called on the United States to set a timetable for withdrawal
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and US coalition partners such as the UK and Denmark began withdrawing their forces from the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The war in Iraq has resulted in
       <a href="/wiki/Casualties_of_the_Iraq_War" title="Casualties of the Iraq War">
        between 151,000 and 1.2 million Iraqis being killed
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="2008.E2.80.93present">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="2008–present">
        2008–present
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/2008_in_Iraq" title="2008 in Iraq">
        2008 in Iraq
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/2009_in_Iraq" title="2009 in Iraq">
        2009 in Iraq
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/2010_in_Iraq" title="2010 in Iraq">
        2010 in Iraq
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/2011_in_Iraq" title="2011 in Iraq">
        2011 in Iraq
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/2012_in_Iraq" title="2012 in Iraq">
        2012 in Iraq
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/2013_in_Iraq" title="2013 in Iraq">
        2013 in Iraq
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/2014_in_Iraq" title="2014 in Iraq">
        2014 in Iraq
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/2015_in_Iraq" title="2015 in Iraq">
        2015 in Iraq
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/2016_in_Iraq" title="2016 in Iraq">
        2016 in Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 2008,
       <a href="/wiki/Iraq_spring_fighting_of_2008" title="Iraq spring fighting of 2008">
        fighting continued
       </a>
       and Iraq's newly trained armed forces launched attacks against militants. The Iraqi government signed the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=US%E2%80%93Iraq_Status_of_Forces_Agreement&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="US–Iraq Status of Forces Agreement (page does not exist)">
        US–Iraq Status of Forces Agreement
       </a>
       , which required US forces to withdraw from Iraqi cities by 30 June 2009 and to withdraw completely from Iraq by 31 December 2011.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iraq_war_map.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3436" data-file-width="3360" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Iraq_war_map.png/220px-Iraq_war_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Iraq_war_map.png/330px-Iraq_war_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Iraq_war_map.png/440px-Iraq_war_map.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iraq_war_map.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The current military situation, 24 October 2017:
         <br/>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #db8ca6; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Controlled by
          <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_Iraq" title="Federal government of Iraq">
           Iraqi government
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #b4b2ae; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Controlled by the
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_State_in_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State in Iraq and the Levant">
           Islamic State in Iraq and the Levant
          </a>
          (ISIL)
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #d7e074; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Controlled by
          <a href="/wiki/Peshmerga" title="Peshmerga">
           Iraqi Kurds
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       US troops handed over security duties to Iraqi forces in June 2009, though they continued to work with Iraqi forces after the pullout.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On the morning of 18 December 2011, the final contingent of US troops to be withdrawn ceremonially exited over the border to
       <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">
        Kuwait
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn-dec11_8-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cnn-dec11-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Crime and violence initially spiked in the months following
       <a href="/wiki/U.S.%E2%80%93Iraq_Status_of_Forces_Agreement" title="U.S.–Iraq Status of Forces Agreement">
        the US withdrawal from cities in mid-2009
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Associated_Press_and_Yahoo.com_97-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-The_Associated_Press_and_Yahoo.com-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but despite the initial increase in violence, in November 2009, Iraqi
       <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Interior_(Iraq)" title="Ministry of Interior (Iraq)">
        Interior Ministry
       </a>
       officials reported that the civilian death toll in Iraq fell to its lowest level since the
       <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">
        2003 invasion
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Following the
       <a href="/wiki/Withdrawal_of_U.S._troops_from_Iraq" title="Withdrawal of U.S. troops from Iraq">
        withdrawal of US troops
       </a>
       in 2011, the insurgency continued and Iraq suffered from political instability. In February 2011, the
       <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">
        Arab Spring
       </a>
       protests
       <a href="/wiki/2011_Iraqi_protests" title="2011 Iraqi protests">
        spread to Iraq
       </a>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but the initial protests did not topple the government. The
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_National_Movement" title="Iraqi National Movement">
        Iraqi National Movement
       </a>
       , reportedly representing the majority of Iraqi Sunnis, boycotted Parliament for several weeks in late 2011 and early 2012, claiming that the Shiite-dominated government was striving to sideline Sunnis.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2012 and 2013, levels of violence increased and armed groups inside Iraq were increasingly galvanised by the
       <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" title="Syrian Civil War">
        Syrian Civil War
       </a>
       . Both Sunnis and Shias crossed the border to fight in Syria.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kurd-Shiite-Sunni-Split_101-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kurd-Shiite-Sunni-Split-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In December 2012, Sunni Arabs
       <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Iraqi_protests" title="2012–13 Iraqi protests">
        protested
       </a>
       against the government, whom they claimed marginalised them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During 2013, Sunni militant groups stepped up attacks targeting the Iraq's Shia population in an attempt to undermine confidence in the
       <a href="/wiki/Nouri_al-Maliki" title="Nouri al-Maliki">
        Nouri al-Maliki
       </a>
       -led government.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes2701_104-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-latimes2701-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2014, Sunni insurgents belonging to the
       <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">
        Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant
       </a>
       (ISIL) terrorist group seized control of large swathes of land including several major Iraqi cities, like
       <a href="/wiki/Tikrit" title="Tikrit">
        Tikrit
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fallujah" title="Fallujah">
        Fallujah
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mosul" title="Mosul">
        Mosul
       </a>
       creating hundreds of thousands of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_persons" title="Internally displaced persons">
        internally displaced persons
       </a>
       amid reports of atrocities by ISIL fighters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After an inconclusive election in April 2014, Nouri al-Maliki served as caretaker-Prime-Minister.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guar11-8-14_106-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-guar11-8-14-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 11 August, Iraq's highest court ruled that PM Maliki's bloc is biggest in parliament, meaning Maliki could stay Prime Minister.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guar11-8-14_106-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-guar11-8-14-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By 13 August, however, the Iraqi president had tasked
       <a href="/wiki/Haider_al-Abadi" title="Haider al-Abadi">
        Haider al-Abadi
       </a>
       with forming a new government, and the United Nations, the United States, the European Union, Saudi Arabia, Iran, and some Iraqi politicians expressed their wish for a new leadership in Iraq, for example from
       <a href="/wiki/Haider_al-Abadi" title="Haider al-Abadi">
        Haider al-Abadi
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 14 August, Maliki stepped down as PM to support Mr al-Abadi and to "safeguard the high interests of the country". The US government welcomed this as "another major step forward" in uniting Iraq.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
        <a href="#cite_note-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 9 September 2014,
       <a href="/wiki/Haider_al-Abadi" title="Haider al-Abadi">
        Haider al-Abadi
       </a>
       had formed a new government and became the new prime minister.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Intermittent conflict between Sunni,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shiite" title="Shiite">
        Shiite
       </a>
       and Kurdish factions has led to increasing debate about the splitting of Iraq into three autonomous regions, including Sunni Kurdistan in the northeast, a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunnistan" title="Sunnistan">
        Sunnistan
       </a>
       in the west and a Shiastan in the southeast.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iraq.A2003060.0750.500m.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2600" data-file-width="2000" height="286" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Iraq.A2003060.0750.500m.jpg/220px-Iraq.A2003060.0750.500m.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Iraq.A2003060.0750.500m.jpg/330px-Iraq.A2003060.0750.500m.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Iraq.A2003060.0750.500m.jpg/440px-Iraq.A2003060.0750.500m.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iraq.A2003060.0750.500m.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Satellite map of Iraq.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iraq_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="1900" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Iraq_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Iraq_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Iraq_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Iraq_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Iraq_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Iraq_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iraq_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Iraq
         <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
          Köppen climate classification
         </a>
         map.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Iraq" title="Geography of Iraq">
        Geography of Iraq
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Governorates_of_Iraq" title="Governorates of Iraq">
        Governorates of Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">

          <b>
           does not
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
            cite
           </a>
           any
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            sources
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iraq&amp;action=edit">

           </a>

           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">

           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">

           </a>
           .
          </span>

           <i>
            (June 2014)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
