      </table>
      <p>
       Iraq lies between latitudes
       <a href="/wiki/29th_parallel_north" title="29th parallel north">
        29°
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/38th_parallel_north" title="38th parallel north">
        38° N
       </a>
       , and longitudes
       <a href="/wiki/39th_meridian_east" title="39th meridian east">
        39°
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/49th_meridian_east" title="49th meridian east">
        49° E
       </a>
       (a small area lies west of 39°). Spanning 437,072 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (168,754 sq mi), it is the 58th-largest country in the world. It is comparable in size to the US state of
       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
        California
       </a>
       , and somewhat larger than
       <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">
        Paraguay
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Iraq mainly consists of
       <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">
        desert
       </a>
       , but near the two major rivers (
       <a href="/wiki/Euphrates" title="Euphrates">
        Euphrates
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tigris" title="Tigris">
        Tigris
       </a>
       ) are fertile
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alluvial_plains" title="Alluvial plains">
        alluvial plains
       </a>
       , as the rivers carry about 60,000,000 m
       <sup>
        3
       </sup>
       (78,477,037 cu yd) of
       <a href="/wiki/Silt" title="Silt">
        silt
       </a>
       annually to the
       <a href="/wiki/River_delta" title="River delta">
        delta
       </a>
       . The north of the country is mostly composed of mountains; the highest point being at 3,611 m (11,847 ft) point, unnamed on the map opposite, but known locally as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cheekah_Dar" title="Cheekah Dar">
        Cheekah Dar
       </a>
       (black tent). Iraq has a small coastline measuring 58 km (36 mi) along the
       <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">
        Persian Gulf
       </a>
       . Close to the coast and along the
       <a href="/wiki/Shatt_al-Arab" title="Shatt al-Arab">
        Shatt al-Arab
       </a>
       (known as
       <i>
        arvandrūd
       </i>
       : اروندرود among Iranians) there used to be marshlands, but many were drained in the 1990s.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Iraq#Climate" title="Geography of Iraq">
        Geography of Iraq § Climate
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Most of Iraq has a hot
       <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">
        arid
       </a>
       climate with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical" title="Subtropical">
        subtropical
       </a>
       influence. Summer temperatures average above 40 °C (104 °F) for most of the country and frequently exceed 48 °C (118.4 °F). Winter temperatures infrequently exceed 21 °C (69.8 °F) with maxima roughly 15 to 19 °C (59.0 to 66.2 °F) and night-time lows 2 to 5 °C (35.6 to 41.0 °F). Typically, precipitation is low; most places receive less than 250 mm (9.8 in) annually, with maximum rainfall occurring during the winter months. Rainfall during the summer is extremely rare, except in the far north of the country. The northern mountainous regions have cold winters with occasional heavy snows, sometimes causing extensive flooding.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">
        Government and politics
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Iraq" title="Politics of Iraq">
        Politics of Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baghdad_Convention_Center_inside.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1960" data-file-width="3008" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Baghdad_Convention_Center_inside.jpg/220px-Baghdad_Convention_Center_inside.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Baghdad_Convention_Center_inside.jpg/330px-Baghdad_Convention_Center_inside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Baghdad_Convention_Center_inside.jpg/440px-Baghdad_Convention_Center_inside.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baghdad_Convention_Center_inside.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Baghdad Convention Center, the current meeting place of the
         <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Representatives_of_Iraq" title="Council of Representatives of Iraq">
          Council of Representatives of Iraq
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_Iraq" title="Federal government of Iraq">
        federal government of Iraq
       </a>
       is defined under the current
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Iraq" title="Constitution of Iraq">
        Constitution
       </a>
       as a
       <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">
        democratic
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">
        federal
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">
        parliamentary
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Islamic_republic" title="Islamic republic">
        Islamic republic
       </a>
       . The federal government is composed of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_branch" title="Executive branch">
        executive
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_branch" title="Legislative branch">
        legislative
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judicial_branch" title="Judicial branch">
        judicial
       </a>
       branches, as well as numerous independent commissions. Aside from the federal government, there are regions (made of one or more governorates), governorates, and districts within Iraq with jurisdiction over various matters as defined by law.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Alliance_(Iraq)" title="National Alliance (Iraq)">
        National Alliance
       </a>
       is the main Shia parliamentary bloc, and was established as a result of a merger of Prime Minister Nouri Maliki's
       <a href="/wiki/State_of_Law_Coalition" title="State of Law Coalition">
        State of Law Coalition
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_National_Alliance" title="Iraqi National Alliance">
        Iraqi National Alliance
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-gpi_111-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-bbc-gpi-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_National_Movement" title="Iraqi National Movement">
        Iraqi National Movement
       </a>
       is led by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iyad_Allawi" title="Iyad Allawi">
        Iyad Allawi
       </a>
       , a secular Shia widely supported by Sunnis. The party has a more consistent anti-sectarian perspective than most of its rivals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-gpi_111-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-bbc-gpi-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan_List" title="Kurdistan List">
        Kurdistan List
       </a>
       is dominated by two parties, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Democratic_Party_(Iraq)" title="Kurdistan Democratic Party (Iraq)">
        Kurdistan Democratic Party
       </a>
       led by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Masood_Barzani" title="Masood Barzani">
        Masood Barzani
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Patriotic_Union_of_Kurdistan" title="Patriotic Union of Kurdistan">
        Patriotic Union of Kurdistan
       </a>
       headed by
       <a href="/wiki/Jalal_Talabani" title="Jalal Talabani">
        Jalal Talabani
       </a>
       . Both parties are secular and enjoy close ties with the West.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-gpi_111-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-bbc-gpi-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2010, according to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Failed_States_Index" title="List of countries by Failed States Index">
        Failed States Index
       </a>
       , Iraq was the world's seventh most politically unstable country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
        <a href="#cite_note-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The concentration of power in the hands of Prime Minister
       <a href="/wiki/Nouri_al-Maliki" title="Nouri al-Maliki">
        Nouri al-Maliki
       </a>
       and growing pressure on the opposition led to growing concern about the future of political rights in Iraq.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fh13_114-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-fh13-114">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nevertheless, progress was made and the country had risen to 11th place by 2013.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
        <a href="#cite_note-115">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In August 2014, al-Maliki's reign came to an end. He announced on 14 August 2014 that he would stand aside so that
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haider_Al-Abadi" title="Haider Al-Abadi">
        Haider Al-Abadi
       </a>
       , who had been nominated just days earlier by newly installed President
       <a href="/wiki/Fuad_Masum" title="Fuad Masum">
        Fuad Masum
       </a>
       , could take over. Until that point, al-Maliki had clung to power even asking the federal court to veto the president's nomination describing it as a violation of the constitution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewPM_116-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NewPM-116">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Transparency International ranks Iraq's government as the eighth-most-corrupt government in the world. Government payroll have increased from 1 million employees under
       <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">
        Saddam Hussein
       </a>
       to around 7 million employees in 2016. In combination with decreased oil prices, the government budget deficit is near 25% of GDP as of 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Since the establishment of the
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_no-fly_zones" title="Iraqi no-fly zones">
        no–fly zones
       </a>
       following the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">
        Gulf War
       </a>
       of 1990–1991, the Kurds established their own
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_area" title="Autonomous area">
        autonomous region
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Law">
        Law
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Iraq" title="Law of Iraq">
        Law of Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In October 2005, the new
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Iraq" title="Constitution of Iraq">
        Constitution of Iraq
       </a>
       was approved in a referendum with a 78% overall majority, although the percentage of support varying widely between the country's territories.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
        <a href="#cite_note-118">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The new constitution was backed by the Shia and Kurdish communities, but was rejected by Arab Sunnis. Under the terms of the constitution, the country conducted
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_parliamentary_election,_December_2005" title="Iraqi parliamentary election, December 2005">
        fresh nationwide parliamentary elections
       </a>
       on 15 December 2005. All three major
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Iraq" title="Ethnic groups in Iraq">
        ethnic groups in Iraq
       </a>
       voted along ethnic lines, as did Assyrian and Turcoman minorities.
      </p>
      <p>
       Law no. 188 of the year 1959 (Personal Status Law)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
        <a href="#cite_note-119">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
       made polygamy extremely difficult, granted child custody to the mother in case of divorce, prohibited repudiation and marriage under the age of 16.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unesco1_120-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-unesco1-120">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Article 1 of Civil Code also identifies Islamic law as a formal source of law.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         [121]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Iraq had no Sharia courts but civil courts used Sharia for issues of personal status including marriage and divorce. In 1995 Iraq introduced Sharia punishment for certain types of criminal offences.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
        <a href="#cite_note-122">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The code is based on French civil law as well as Sunni and Jafari (Shi'ite) interpretations of Sharia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
        <a href="#cite_note-123">
         [123]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2004, the
       <a href="/wiki/Coalition_Provisional_Authority" title="Coalition Provisional Authority">
        CPA
       </a>
       chief executive L. Paul Bremer said he would veto any constitutional draft stating that sharia is the principal basis of law.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
        <a href="#cite_note-124">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The declaration enraged many local Shia clerics,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
        <a href="#cite_note-125">
         [125]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and by 2005 the United States had relented, allowing a role for sharia in the constitution to help end a stalemate on the draft constitution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
        <a href="#cite_note-126">
         [126]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Penal_Code" title="Iraqi Penal Code">
        Iraqi Penal Code
       </a>
       is the statutory law of Iraq.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Military">
        Military
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Armed_Forces" title="Iraqi Armed Forces">
        Iraqi Armed Forces
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BMP-1_Iraq_3.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1312" data-file-width="2000" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/BMP-1_Iraq_3.jpg/220px-BMP-1_Iraq_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/BMP-1_Iraq_3.jpg/330px-BMP-1_Iraq_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/BMP-1_Iraq_3.jpg/440px-BMP-1_Iraq_3.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BMP-1_Iraq_3.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An Iraqi Army BMP-1 on the move.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Iraqi security forces are composed of forces serving under the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Interior" title="Ministry of Interior">
        Ministry of Interior
       </a>
       (which controls the
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Police" title="Iraqi Police">
        Police
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Popular_Mobilization_Forces" title="Popular Mobilization Forces">
        Popular Mobilization Forces
       </a>
       ) and the
       <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Iraq)" title="Ministry of Defence (Iraq)">
        Ministry of Defense
       </a>
       , as well as the Iraqi
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Counter_Terrorism_Bureau" title="Counter Terrorism Bureau">
        Counter Terrorism Bureau
       </a>
       , reporting directly to the
       <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Iraq" title="Prime Minister of Iraq">
        Prime Minister of Iraq
       </a>
       , which oversees the
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Special_Operations_Forces" title="Iraqi Special Operations Forces">
        Iraqi Special Operations Forces
       </a>
       . Ministry of Defense forces include the
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Army" title="Iraqi Army">
        Iraqi Army
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Air_Force" title="Iraqi Air Force">
        Iraqi Air Force
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Navy" title="Iraqi Navy">
        Iraqi Navy
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Peshmerga" title="Peshmerga">
        Peshmerga
       </a>
       are a separate armed force loyal to the
       <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Regional_Government" title="Kurdistan Regional Government">
        Kurdistan Regional Government
       </a>
       . The regional government and the central government disagree as to whether they are under Baghdad's authority and to what extent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
        <a href="#cite_note-127">
         [127]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Army" title="Iraqi Army">
        Iraqi Army
       </a>
       is an objective counter-insurgency force that as of November 2009 includes 14 divisions, each division consisting of 4 brigades.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ltcolswanson-040308_128-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ltcolswanson-040308-128">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is described as the most important element of the counter-insurgency fight.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_New_Iraqi_Security_Forces_129-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-The_New_Iraqi_Security_Forces-129">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Light infantry brigades are equipped with small arms, machine guns, RPGs, body armour and light armoured vehicles. Mechanized infantry brigades are equipped with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T-54/55" title="T-54/55">
        T-54/55
       </a>
       main battle tanks and
       <a href="/wiki/BMP-1" title="BMP-1">
        BMP-1
       </a>
       infantry fighting vehicles.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_New_Iraqi_Security_Forces_129-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-The_New_Iraqi_Security_Forces-129">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of mid-2008, logistical problems included a maintenance crisis and ongoing supply problems.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
        <a href="#cite_note-130">
         [130]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Air_Force" title="Iraqi Air Force">
        Iraqi Air Force
       </a>
       is designed to support ground forces with surveillance, reconnaissance and troop lift. Two reconnaissance squadrons use light aircraft, three helicopter squadrons are used to move troops and one air transportation squadron uses C-130 transport aircraft to move troops, equipment, and supplies. It currently has 3,000 personnel. It is planned to increase to 18,000 personnel, with 550 aircraft by 2018.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_New_Iraqi_Security_Forces_129-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-The_New_Iraqi_Security_Forces-129">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Navy" title="Iraqi Navy">
        Iraqi Navy
       </a>
       is a small force with 1,500 sailors and officers, including 800
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marines_(military)" title="Marines (military)">
        Marines
       </a>
       , designed to protect shoreline and inland waterways from insurgent infiltration. The navy is also responsible for the security of offshore oil platforms. The navy will have coastal patrol squadrons, assault boat squadrons and a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marines_(military)" title="Marines (military)">
        marine
       </a>
       battalion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_New_Iraqi_Security_Forces_129-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-The_New_Iraqi_Security_Forces-129">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The force will consist of 2,000 to 2,500 sailors by year 2010.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSR070321_131-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-WSR070321-131">
         [131]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">
        Foreign relations
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Iraq" title="Foreign relations of Iraq">
        Foreign relations of Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_%26_Jalal_Talabani_in_Baghdad_4-7-09.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2273" data-file-width="3410" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Barack_Obama_%26_Jalal_Talabani_in_Baghdad_4-7-09.JPG/220px-Barack_Obama_%26_Jalal_Talabani_in_Baghdad_4-7-09.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Barack_Obama_%26_Jalal_Talabani_in_Baghdad_4-7-09.JPG/330px-Barack_Obama_%26_Jalal_Talabani_in_Baghdad_4-7-09.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Barack_Obama_%26_Jalal_Talabani_in_Baghdad_4-7-09.JPG/440px-Barack_Obama_%26_Jalal_Talabani_in_Baghdad_4-7-09.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_%26_Jalal_Talabani_in_Baghdad_4-7-09.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         US President
         <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">
          Barack Obama
         </a>
         speaking with
         <a href="/wiki/President_of_Iraq" title="President of Iraq">
          Iraqi President
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Jalal_Talabani" title="Jalal Talabani">
          Jalal Talabani
         </a>
         in 2009.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg">
          <img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>
         </a>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          <b>
           This section needs expansion
          </b>
          .
          <small>
           You can help by
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iraq&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">
            adding to it
           </a>
           .
          </small>
          <small>
           <i>
            (June 2012)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       On 17 November 2008, the US and Iraq agreed to a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Status_of_Forces_Agreement" title="Status of Forces Agreement">
        Status of Forces Agreement
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
        <a href="#cite_note-132">
         [132]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as part of the broader
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strategic_Framework_Agreement" title="Strategic Framework Agreement">
        Strategic Framework Agreement
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
        <a href="#cite_note-133">
         [133]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This agreement states "the Government of Iraq requests" US forces to temporarily remain in Iraq to "maintain security and stability" and that Iraq has jurisdiction over military contractors, and US personnel when not on US bases or on–duty.
      </p>
      <p>
       On 12 February 2009, Iraq officially became the 186th State Party to the
       <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Weapons_Convention" title="Chemical Weapons Convention">
        Chemical Weapons Convention
       </a>
       . Under the provisions of this
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty" title="Treaty">
        treaty
       </a>
       , Iraq is considered a party with declared
       <a href="/wiki/Stockpile" title="Stockpile">
        stockpiles
       </a>
       of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chemical_weapons" title="Chemical weapons">
        chemical weapons
       </a>
       . Because of their late accession, Iraq is the only State Party exempt from the existing timeline for destruction of their chemical weapons. Specific criteria is in development to address the unique nature of Iraqi accession.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
        <a href="#cite_note-134">
         [134]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_relations" title="Iran–Iraq relations">
        Iran–Iraq relations
       </a>
       have flourished since 2005 by the exchange of high level visits: Iraqi PM Nouri al-Maliki made frequent visits to Iran, along with Jalal Talabani visiting numerous times, to help boost bilateral co-operation in all fields.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       A conflict occurred in December 2009, when Iraq accused Iran of seizing an oil well on the border.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
        <a href="#cite_note-135">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Iraq%E2%80%93Turkey_relations" title="Iraq–Turkey relations">
        Relationships with Turkey
       </a>
       are tense, largely because of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Regional_Government" title="Kurdistan Regional Government">
        Kurdistan Regional Government
       </a>
       , as clashes between Turkey and the
       <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Workers%27_Party" title="Kurdistan Workers' Party">
        PKK
       </a>
       continue.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
        <a href="#cite_note-136">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In October 2011, the Turkish parliament renewed a law that gives Turkish forces the ability to pursue rebels over the border in Iraq."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
        <a href="#cite_note-137">
         [137]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">
        Human rights
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Iraq" title="Human rights in Iraq">
        Human rights in Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Relations between Iraq and its
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Kurdistan" title="Iraqi Kurdistan">
        Kurdish population
       </a>
       have been sour in recent history, especially with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Anfal_Campaign" title="Al-Anfal Campaign">
        Saddam Hussein's genocidal campaign
       </a>
       against them in the 1980s. After
       <a href="/wiki/1991_uprisings_in_Iraq" title="1991 uprisings in Iraq">
        uprisings during the early 90s
       </a>
       , many Kurds fled their homeland and
       <a href="/wiki/No-fly_zone" title="No-fly zone">
        no-fly zones
       </a>
       were established in northern Iraq to prevent more conflicts. Despite historically poor relations, some progress has been made, and Iraq elected its first Kurdish president,
       <a href="/wiki/Jalal_Talabani" title="Jalal Talabani">
        Jalal Talabani
       </a>
       , in 2005. Furthermore,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kurdish_language" title="Kurdish language">
        Kurdish
       </a>
       is now an official language of Iraq alongside
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
        Arabic
       </a>
       according to Article 4 of the constitution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIraqi_ConstitutionArticle_4_138-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIraqi_ConstitutionArticle_4-138">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Iraq" title="LGBT rights in Iraq">
        LGBT rights in Iraq
       </a>
       remain limited. Although
       <a href="/wiki/Sodomy_law" title="Sodomy law">
        decriminalised
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">
        homosexuality
       </a>
       remains
       <a href="/wiki/Homophobia" title="Homophobia">
        stigmatised in Iraqi society
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
        <a href="#cite_note-139">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Targeting people because of their gender identity or sexual orientation is not uncommon and is usually carried out in the name of
       <a href="/wiki/Honor_killing" title="Honor killing">
        family honour
       </a>
       . People who dress in
       <a href="/wiki/Emo" title="Emo">
        emo
       </a>
       style are mistakenly associated with homosexuality and may suffer the same fate.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
        <a href="#cite_note-140">
         [140]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Investigations by the BBC and other western media in 2008 and 2009, including interviews of homosexual and transgender Iraqis, showed that violence against LGBT people had significantly increased since Saddam Hussein was toppled.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
        <a href="#cite_note-141">
         [141]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
        <a href="#cite_note-142">
         [142]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
        <a href="#cite_note-143">
         [143]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
        <a href="#cite_note-144">
         [144]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
        <a href="#cite_note-145">
         [145]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">
        Administrative divisions
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Governorates_of_Iraq" title="Governorates of Iraq">
        Governorates of Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="floatright">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iraq,_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg">
        <img alt="Iraq, administrative divisions - Nmbrs - colored.svg" data-file-height="1264" data-file-width="1241" height="306" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Iraq%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/300px-Iraq%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Iraq%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/450px-Iraq%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Iraq%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/600px-Iraq%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Iraq is composed of nineteen
       <a href="/wiki/Governorate" title="Governorate">
        governorates
       </a>
       (or
       <a href="/wiki/Province" title="Province">
        provinces
       </a>
       ) (Arabic:
       <i>
        muhafadhat
       </i>
       (singular
       <i>
        muhafadhah
       </i>
       ); Kurdish: پارێزگا
       <i>
        Pârizgah
       </i>
       ). The governorates are subdivided into
       <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Iraq" title="Districts of Iraq">
        districts
       </a>
       (or
       <i>
        qadhas
       </i>
       ), which are further divided into
       <a href="/wiki/Nahiyah" title="Nahiyah">
        sub-districts
       </a>
       (or
       <i>
        nawāḥī
       </i>
       ).
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Kurdistan" title="Iraqi Kurdistan">
        Iraqi Kurdistan
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Erbil_Governorate" title="Erbil Governorate">
        Erbil
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dohuk_Governorate" title="Dohuk Governorate">
        Dohuk
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/As_Sulaymaniyah_Governorate" title="As Sulaymaniyah Governorate">
        Sulaymaniyah
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Halabja_Governorate" title="Halabja Governorate">
        Halabja
       </a>
       ) is the only legally defined region within Iraq, with its own
       <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Regional_Government" title="Kurdistan Regional Government">
        government
       </a>
       and quasi-official army
       <a href="/wiki/Peshmerga" title="Peshmerga">
        Peshmerga
       </a>
       .
      </p>

         </a>
        </li>

         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dhi_Qar_Province" title="Dhi Qar Province">

         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basra_Province" title="Basra Province">
          Basra
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Halabja_Governorate" title="Halabja Governorate">
          Halabja
         </a>
         (not shown)
        </li>

      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Iraq" title="Economy of Iraq">
        Economy of Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iraq_GDP_per_capita_1950-2008.png">
         <img alt="Graph of Iraqi GNP, showing highest GNP in 1980" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="237" data-file-width="310" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Iraq_GDP_per_capita_1950-2008.png/220px-Iraq_GDP_per_capita_1950-2008.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8d/Iraq_GDP_per_capita_1950-2008.png 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iraq_GDP_per_capita_1950-2008.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         GNP per capita in Iraq from 1950 to 2008.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2006Iraqi_exports.PNG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" height="96" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/2006Iraqi_exports.PNG/220px-2006Iraqi_exports.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/2006Iraqi_exports.PNG/330px-2006Iraqi_exports.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/2006Iraqi_exports.PNG/440px-2006Iraqi_exports.PNG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2006Iraqi_exports.PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Global distribution of Iraqi exports in 2006.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Iraq's economy is dominated by the
       <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">
        oil
       </a>
       sector, which has traditionally provided about 95% of foreign exchange earnings. The lack of development in other sectors has resulted in 18%–30% unemployed and a depressed per capita GDP of $4,000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_146-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-146">
         [146]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Public sector employment accounted for nearly 60% of full-time employment in 2011.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usaid11_147-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-usaid11-147">
         [147]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The oil export industry, which dominates the Iraqi economy, generates very little employment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usaid11_147-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-usaid11-147">
         [147]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Currently only a modest percentage of women (the highest estimate for 2011 was 22%) participate in the labour force.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usaid11_147-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-usaid11-147">
         [147]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Prior to US occupation, Iraq's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centrally_planned_economy" title="Centrally planned economy">
        centrally planned economy
       </a>
       prohibited foreign ownership of Iraqi businesses, ran most large industries as state-owned enterprises, and imposed large
       <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">
        tariffs
       </a>
       to keep out foreign goods.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
        <a href="#cite_note-148">
         [148]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2003_Invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 Invasion of Iraq">
        2003 Invasion of Iraq
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Coalition_Provisional_Authority" title="Coalition Provisional Authority">
        Coalition Provisional Authority
       </a>
       quickly began issuing many binding orders
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Privatisation" title="Privatisation">
        privatising
       </a>
       Iraq's economy and opening it up to
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">
        foreign investment
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iraqi_Kurdish_villagers_in_field_near_Turkish_border.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="2458" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Iraqi_Kurdish_villagers_in_field_near_Turkish_border.jpg/220px-Iraqi_Kurdish_villagers_in_field_near_Turkish_border.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Iraqi_Kurdish_villagers_in_field_near_Turkish_border.jpg/330px-Iraqi_Kurdish_villagers_in_field_near_Turkish_border.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Iraqi_Kurdish_villagers_in_field_near_Turkish_border.jpg/440px-Iraqi_Kurdish_villagers_in_field_near_Turkish_border.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iraqi_Kurdish_villagers_in_field_near_Turkish_border.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Agriculture is the main occupation of the people.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On November 20, 2004, the
       <a href="/wiki/Paris_Club" title="Paris Club">
        Paris Club
       </a>
       of creditor nations agreed to write off 80% ($33 billion) of Iraq's $42 billion debt to Club members. Iraq's total external debt was around $120 billion at the time of the 2003 invasion, and had grown another $5 billion by 2004. The
       <a href="/wiki/Debt_relief" title="Debt relief">
        debt relief
       </a>
       will be implemented in three stages: two of 30% each and one of 20%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">
        <a href="#cite_note-149">
         [149]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In February 2011,
       <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">
        Citigroup
       </a>
       included Iraq in a group of countries which it described as
       <a href="/wiki/3G_(countries)" title="3G (countries)">
        'Global Growth Generators'
       </a>
       , that it argued will enjoy significant economic growth in the future.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
        <a href="#cite_note-150">
         [150]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The official currency in Iraq is the
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_dinar" title="Iraqi dinar">
        Iraqi dinar
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Coalition_Provisional_Authority" title="Coalition Provisional Authority">
        Coalition Provisional Authority
       </a>
       issued new dinar coins and notes, with the notes printed by
       <a href="/wiki/De_La_Rue" title="De La Rue">
        De La Rue
       </a>
       using modern anti-forgery techniques.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
        <a href="#cite_note-151">
         [151]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Jim_Cramer" title="Jim Cramer">
        Jim Cramer
       </a>
       's October 20, 2009 endorsement of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_Dinar" title="Iraqi Dinar">
        Iraqi Dinar
       </a>
       on
       <a href="/wiki/CNBC" title="CNBC">
        CNBC
       </a>
       has further piqued interest in the investment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jim_Cramer_on_the_Iraqi_Dinar_152-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Jim_Cramer_on_the_Iraqi_Dinar-152">
         [152]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Five years after the invasion, an estimated 2.4 million people were
       <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_person" title="Internally displaced person">
        internally displaced
       </a>
       (with a further two million refugees outside Iraq), four million Iraqis were considered food-insecure (a quarter of children were chronically malnourished) and only a third of Iraqi children had access to safe drinking water.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI1_153-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ODI1-153">
         [153]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Development_Institute" title="Overseas Development Institute">
        Overseas Development Institute
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_NGO" title="International NGO">
        international NGOs
       </a>
       face challenges in carrying out their mission, leaving their assistance "piecemeal and largely conducted undercover, hindered by insecurity, a lack of coordinated funding, limited operational capacity and patchy information".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI1_153-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ODI1-153">
         [153]
        </a>
       </sup>
       International NGOs have been targeted and during the first 5 years, 94 aid workers were killed, 248 injured, 24 arrested or detained and 89 kidnapped or abducted.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI1_153-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-ODI1-153">
         [153]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_and_energy">
        Oil and energy
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves_in_Iraq" title="Oil reserves in Iraq">
        Oil reserves in Iraq
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Iraq" title="Energy in Iraq">
        Energy in Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tankers_at_the_Iraqi_Al_Basra_Oil_Terminal_in_the_Northern_Arabian_Gulf.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2100" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Tankers_at_the_Iraqi_Al_Basra_Oil_Terminal_in_the_Northern_Arabian_Gulf.jpg/220px-Tankers_at_the_Iraqi_Al_Basra_Oil_Terminal_in_the_Northern_Arabian_Gulf.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Tankers_at_the_Iraqi_Al_Basra_Oil_Terminal_in_the_Northern_Arabian_Gulf.jpg/330px-Tankers_at_the_Iraqi_Al_Basra_Oil_Terminal_in_the_Northern_Arabian_Gulf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Tankers_at_the_Iraqi_Al_Basra_Oil_Terminal_in_the_Northern_Arabian_Gulf.jpg/440px-Tankers_at_the_Iraqi_Al_Basra_Oil_Terminal_in_the_Northern_Arabian_Gulf.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tankers_at_the_Iraqi_Al_Basra_Oil_Terminal_in_the_Northern_Arabian_Gulf.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Tankers at the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basra_Oil_Terminal" title="Basra Oil Terminal">
          Basra Oil Terminal
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       With its 143.1 billion barrels (2.275
       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">
        ×
       </span>
       10
       <sup>
        10
       </sup>
       m
       <sup>
        3
       </sup>
       ) of proved oil reserves, Iraq ranks third in the world behind Venezuela and Saudi Arabia in the amount of
       <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves" title="Oil reserves">
        oil reserves
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
        <a href="#cite_note-154">
         [154]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
        <a href="#cite_note-155">
         [155]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Oil production levels reached 3.4 million barrels per day by December 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">
        <a href="#cite_note-156">
         [156]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Only about 2,000
       <a href="/wiki/Oil_well" title="Oil well">
        oil wells
       </a>
       have been drilled in Iraq, compared with about 1 million wells in
       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">
        Texas
       </a>
       alone.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
        <a href="#cite_note-157">
         [157]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Iraq was one of the founding members of
       <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">
        OPEC
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
        <a href="#cite_note-158">
         [158]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
        <a href="#cite_note-159">
         [159]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As of 2010
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iraq&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , despite improved security and billions of dollars in oil revenue, Iraq still generates about half the electricity that customers demand, leading to protests during the hot summer months.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
        <a href="#cite_note-160">
         [160]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraq_oil_law" title="Iraq oil law">
        Iraq oil law
       </a>
       , a proposed piece of legislation submitted to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_Council_of_Representatives" title="Iraqi Council of Representatives">
        Iraqi Council of Representatives
       </a>
       in 2007, has failed to gain approval due to disagreements among Iraq's various political blocs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">
        <a href="#cite_note-161">
         [161]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">
        <a href="#cite_note-162">
         [162]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to a US Study from May 2007, between 100,000 barrels per day (16,000 m
       <sup>
        3
       </sup>
       /d) and 300,000 barrels per day (48,000 m
       <sup>
        3
       </sup>
       /d) of Iraq's declared oil production over the past four years could have been siphoned off through corruption or smuggling.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
        <a href="#cite_note-163">
         [163]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2008, Al Jazeera reported $13 billion of Iraqi oil revenues in US care was improperly accounted for, of which $2.6 billion is totally unaccounted for.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">
        <a href="#cite_note-164">
         [164]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some reports that the government has reduced corruption in public procurement of oil; however, reliable reports of bribery and kickbacks to government officials continue to persist.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">
        <a href="#cite_note-165">
         [165]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In June 2008, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_Oil_Ministry" title="Iraqi Oil Ministry">
        Iraqi Oil Ministry
       </a>
       announced plans to go ahead with small one- or two-year
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/No-bid_contracts" title="No-bid contracts">
        no-bid contracts
       </a>
       to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exxon_Mobil" title="Exxon Mobil">
        Exxon Mobil
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">
        Shell
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Total_S.A." title="Total S.A.">
        Total
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">
        BP
       </a>
       —once partners in the
       <a href="/wiki/Iraq_Petroleum_Company" title="Iraq Petroleum Company">
        Iraq Petroleum Company
       </a>
       —along with
       <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">
        Chevron
       </a>
       and smaller firms to service Iraq's largest fields.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
        <a href="#cite_note-166">
         [166]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These plans were cancelled in September because negotiations had stalled for so long that the work could not be completed within the time frame, according to Iraqi oil minister
       <a href="/wiki/Hussain_al-Shahristani" title="Hussain al-Shahristani">
        Hussain al-Shahristani
       </a>
       . Several United States senators had also criticised the deal, arguing it was hindering efforts to pass the hydrocarbon law.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">
        <a href="#cite_note-167">
         [167]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 30 June and 11 December 2009, the
       <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Oil_(Iraq)" title="Ministry of Oil (Iraq)">
        Iraqi ministry of oil
       </a>
       awarded service contracts to international oil companies for some of Iraq's many oil fields.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera091211_168-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-aljazeera091211-168">
         [168]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera090630_169-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-aljazeera090630-169">
         [169]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Oil fields contracted include the "super-giant"
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Majnoon_Field" title="Majnoon Field">
        Majnoon Field
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Halfaya_Field" title="Halfaya Field">
        Halfaya Field
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/West_Qurna_Field" title="West Qurna Field">
        West Qurna Field
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Rumaila_oil_field" title="Rumaila oil field">
        Rumaila Field
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera090630_169-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-aljazeera090630-169">
         [169]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">
        BP
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/China_National_Petroleum_Corporation" title="China National Petroleum Corporation">
        China National Petroleum Corporation
       </a>
       won a deal to develop Rumaila, the largest Iraqi oil field.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
        <a href="#cite_note-170">
         [170]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">
        <a href="#cite_note-171">
         [171]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 14 March 2014, the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">
        International Energy Agency
       </a>
       said Iraq's oil output jumped by half a million barrels a day in February to average 3.6 million barrels a day. The country hadn't pumped that much oil since 1979, when Saddam Hussein rose to power.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">
        <a href="#cite_note-172">
         [172]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, on 14 July 2014, as sectarian strife had taken hold,
       <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Regional_Government" title="Kurdistan Regional Government">
        Kurdistan Regional Government
       </a>
       forces seized control of the Bai Hassan and
       <a href="/wiki/Kirkuk_Field" title="Kirkuk Field">
        Kirkuk
       </a>
       oilfields in the north of the country, taking them from Iraq's control. Baghdad condemned the seizure and threatened "dire consequences" if the fields were not returned.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KurdsOilfields_173-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-KurdsOilfields-173">
         [173]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">
        Water supply and sanitation
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20160104-Lake_in_Samawa_desert_Iraq_0356.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5760" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/20160104-Lake_in_Samawa_desert_Iraq_0356.jpg/220px-20160104-Lake_in_Samawa_desert_Iraq_0356.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/20160104-Lake_in_Samawa_desert_Iraq_0356.jpg/330px-20160104-Lake_in_Samawa_desert_Iraq_0356.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/20160104-Lake_in_Samawa_desert_Iraq_0356.jpg/440px-20160104-Lake_in_Samawa_desert_Iraq_0356.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20160104-Lake_in_Samawa_desert_Iraq_0356.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A reservoir in the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samawa" title="Samawa">
          Samawa
         </a>
         desert Southern Iraq
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Iraq" title="Water supply and sanitation in Iraq">
        Water supply and sanitation in Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">
        Water supply
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">
        sanitation
       </a>
       in Iraq is characterized by poor
       <a href="/wiki/Water_quality" title="Water quality">
        water
       </a>
       and service quality. Three decades of war, combined with limited environmental awareness, have destroyed Iraq's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_resources_management" title="Water resources management">
        water resources management
       </a>
       system. Access to potable water differs significantly among governorates and between urban and rural areas. 91% of the entire population has access to potable water. But in rural areas, only 77% of the population has access to improved drinking water sources compared to 98% in urban areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNWater_174-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-UNWater-174">
         [174]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Large amounts of water are wasted during production.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNWater_174-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-UNWater-174">
         [174]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">
        Infrastructure
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mosul_Dam_USACE_NWD.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="364" data-file-width="976" height="82" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Mosul_Dam_USACE_NWD.jpg/220px-Mosul_Dam_USACE_NWD.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Mosul_Dam_USACE_NWD.jpg/330px-Mosul_Dam_USACE_NWD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Mosul_Dam_USACE_NWD.jpg/440px-Mosul_Dam_USACE_NWD.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mosul_Dam_USACE_NWD.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Mosul_Dam" title="Mosul Dam">
          Mosul Dam
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Although many infrastructure projects are underway, Iraq remains in deep housing crisis, with the war-ravaged country likely to complete only 5 percent of the 2.5 million homes it needs to build by 2016 to keep up with demand, the Minister for Construction and Housing said in September 2013.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175">
        <a href="#cite_note-175">
         [175]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        In 2009, the IBBC was established (
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.webuildiraq.org/" rel="nofollow">
         Iraq Britain Business Council
        </a>
        ). The Council was established by
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baroness_Nicholson_of_Winterbourne" title="Baroness Nicholson of Winterbourne">
         Baroness Nicholson of Winterbourne
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        In August 2009, two American firms reached a deal with the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_Government" title="Iraqi Government">
         Iraqi Government
        </a>
        to build
        <a href="/wiki/Basra_Sports_City" title="Basra Sports City">
         Basra Sports City
        </a>
        , a new sports complex.
       </li>
       <li>
        In October 2012, the Emirati property firm,
        <a href="/wiki/Emaar_Properties" title="Emaar Properties">
         Emaar Properties
        </a>
        reached a deal with the Iraqi Ministry of Construction and Housing to build and develop housing and commercial projects in Iraq.
       </li>
       <li>
        In January 2013, the Emirati property firm,
        <a href="/wiki/Nakheel_Properties" title="Nakheel Properties">
         Nakheel Properties
        </a>
        signed a deal to build Al Nakheel City, a future town in
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basra,_Iraq" title="Basra, Iraq">
         Basra, Iraq
        </a>
        .
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Iraq" title="Demographics of Iraq">
        Demographics of Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0 0 1em 1em;">

      <p>
       The 2016 estimate of the total Iraqi population is 37,202,572.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Iraq's population was estimated to be 2 million in 1878.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Issawi1988_176-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Issawi1988-176">
         [176]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2013 Iraq's population reached 35 million amid a post-war population boom.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179">
        <a href="#cite_note-179">
         [179]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">
        Ethnic groups
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">
        Arabs
       </a>
       form 75%–80% of the population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_146-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-146">
         [146]
        </a>
       </sup>
       15% of Iraq's population are
       <a href="/wiki/Kurds" title="Kurds">
        Kurds
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrian_People" title="Assyrian People">
        Assyrians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Turkmens" title="Iraqi Turkmens">
        Iraqi Turkmen/Turkoman
       </a>
       and other much smaller minorities, such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mandeans" title="Mandeans">
        Mandeans
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armenian_people" title="Armenian people">
        Armenians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Circassians" title="Circassians">
        Circassians
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iranian_people" title="Iranian people">
        Iranians
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shabaki" title="Shabaki">
        Shabakis
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Yazidis" title="Yazidis">
        Yazidis
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kawliya" title="Kawliya">
        Kawliya
       </a>
       , make up the remainder 5%–10% of the population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_146-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-146">
         [146]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180">
        <a href="#cite_note-180">
         [180]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Around 20,000
       <a href="/wiki/Marsh_Arabs" title="Marsh Arabs">
        Marsh Arabs
       </a>
       live in southern Iraq.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181">
        <a href="#cite_note-181">
         [181]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Iraq has a community of 2,500
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chechen_people" title="Chechen people">
        Chechens
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182">
        <a href="#cite_note-182">
         [182]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In southern Iraq,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro_Iraqis" title="Afro Iraqis">
        there is a community of Iraqis of African
       </a>
       descent, a legacy of the
       <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">
        slavery
       </a>
       practised in the Islamic Caliphate beginning before the
       <a href="/wiki/Zanj_Rebellion" title="Zanj Rebellion">
        Zanj Rebellion
       </a>
       of the 9th century, and
       <a href="/wiki/Basra" title="Basra">
        Basra
       </a>
       's role as a key port.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zanj_53-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-zanj-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is the most populous country in the
       <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Plate" title="Arabian Plate">
        Arabian Plate
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183">
        <a href="#cite_note-183">
         [183]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
        Languages
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Iraq" title="Languages of Iraq">
        Languages of Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Children_puppy_sulaimania.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1436" data-file-width="1808" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Children_puppy_sulaimania.jpg/220px-Children_puppy_sulaimania.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Children_puppy_sulaimania.jpg/330px-Children_puppy_sulaimania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Children_puppy_sulaimania.jpg/440px-Children_puppy_sulaimania.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Children_puppy_sulaimania.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kurdish_people" title="Kurdish people">
          Kurdish
         </a>
         children in
         <a href="/wiki/Sulaymaniyah" title="Sulaymaniyah">
          Sulaymaniyah
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
        Arabic
       </a>
       is the majority language;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kurdish_language" title="Kurdish language">
        Kurdish
       </a>
       is spoken by approximately 10–15% of the population; and
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Turkmens#Language" title="Iraqi Turkmens">
        Turkmen/Turkoman
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIraqi_ConstitutionArticle_4_138-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIraqi_ConstitutionArticle_4-138">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-Aramaic" title="Neo-Aramaic">
        Neo-Aramaic
       </a>
       language of the
       <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">
        Assyrians
       </a>
       and others, by 5%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_146-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-146">
         [146]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other smaller minority languages include
       <a href="/wiki/Mandaic_language" title="Mandaic language">
        Mandaic
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shabaki_language" title="Shabaki language">
        Shabaki
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">
        Armenian
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Circassian_language" title="Circassian language">
        Circassian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">
        Persian
       </a>
       . Arabic, Kurdish, Persian, and Turkmen/Turkoman are written with versions of the
       <a href="/wiki/Arabic_script" title="Arabic script">
        Arabic script
       </a>
       , the Neo-Aramaic languages in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syriac_script" title="Syriac script">
        Syriac script
       </a>
       and Armenian is written in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armenian_script" title="Armenian script">
        Armenian script
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Prior to the invasion in 2003,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
        Arabic
       </a>
       was the sole official language. Since the new
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Iraq" title="Constitution of Iraq">
        Constitution of Iraq
       </a>
       approved in June 2004, both Arabic and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kurdish_language" title="Kurdish language">
        Kurdish
       </a>
       are official languages,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIraqi_ConstitutionArticle_4,_1st_section_184-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIraqi_ConstitutionArticle_4,_1st_section-184">
         [184]
        </a>
       </sup>
       while
       <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_Neo-Aramaic" title="Assyrian Neo-Aramaic">
        Assyrian Neo-Aramaic
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Turkmens#Language" title="Iraqi Turkmens">
        Turkmen/Turkoman language
       </a>
       (referred to as respectively "Syriac" and "Turkmen" in the constitution) are recognised regional languages.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIraqi_ConstitutionArticle_4,_4th_section_185-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIraqi_ConstitutionArticle_4,_4th_section-185">
         [185]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition, any region or province may declare other languages official if a majority of the population approves in a general referendum.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIraqi_ConstitutionArticle_4,_5th_section_186-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIraqi_ConstitutionArticle_4,_5th_section-186">
         [186]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_constitution" title="Iraqi constitution">
        Iraqi constitution
       </a>
       :
      </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>
        The Arabic language and the Kurdish language are the two official languages of Iraq. The right of Iraqis to educate their children in their mother tongue, such as Turkmen, Assyrian, and Armenian shall be guaranteed in government educational institutions in accordance with educational guidelines, or in any other language in private educational institutions.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Iraqi_Constitution_187-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Iraqi_Constitution-187">
          [187]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </p>
      </blockquote>

        <td style="text-align:right;">
         1,100,000
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">
