      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Iraq" title="Religion in Iraq">
        Religion in Iraq
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Iraq" title="Islam in Iraq">
        Islam in Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
        <table style="border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">
         <tr style="background:#ddd">
          <th colspan="5">
           Religion in Iraq, 2014
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188">
            <a href="#cite_note-188">
             [188]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </th>
         </tr>
         <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">
          <td style="padding:0 4px;">
          </td>
          <td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;">
          </td>
          <td style="width:100px;">
          </td>
          <td style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;">
          </td>
          <td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;">
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">
            Shia Islam
           </a>
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:lime; width:64.5%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           64.5%
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">
            Sunni Islam
           </a>
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:green; width:31.5%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           31.5%
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           <a href="/wiki/Gnosticism" title="Gnosticism">
            Gnosticism
           </a>
           /
           <a href="/wiki/Yazd%C3%A2nism" title="Yazdânism">
            Yazdânism
           </a>
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:brown; width:2.0%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           2.0%
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
            Christianity
           </a>
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:red; width:1.2%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           1.2%
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           Other religion
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:orange; width:0.8%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           0.8%
          </td>
         </tr>
        </table>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ImamAliMosqueNajafIraq.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="994" data-file-width="1404" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/ImamAliMosqueNajafIraq.JPG/220px-ImamAliMosqueNajafIraq.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/ImamAliMosqueNajafIraq.JPG/330px-ImamAliMosqueNajafIraq.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/ImamAliMosqueNajafIraq.JPG/440px-ImamAliMosqueNajafIraq.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ImamAliMosqueNajafIraq.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Imam_Ali_Mosque" title="Imam Ali Mosque">
          Imam Ali Mosque
         </a>
         in Najaf.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Muslim (official) 99% (Shia 55-60%, Sunni 40%), Christian &lt;.1%, Yazidi &lt;.1%, Sabean Mandaean &lt;.1%, Baha'i &lt;.1%, Zoroastrian &lt;.1%, Hindu &lt;0.1%, Buddhist &lt;0.1%, Jewish &lt;0.1%, folk religion &lt;0.1, unafilliated 0.1%, other &lt;0.1%
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_146-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-146">
         [146]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It has a mixed
       <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">
        Shia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">
        Sunni
       </a>
       population. The CIA World Factbook estimates that around 65% of Muslims in Iraq are Shia, and around 35% are Sunni.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_146-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-146">
         [146]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A 2011 Pew Research Center estimates that 51% of Muslims in Iraq are Shia, 42% are Sunni, while 5% identify themselves as "Just a Muslim".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189">
        <a href="#cite_note-189">
         [189]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Sunni Muslims, 12-13 million in a population of 36 million, include Arabs, most Turkomen, and Kurds.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Sunni population complains of facing discrimination in almost all aspects of life by the government. However, Prime Minister Nouri al-Maliki has denied that such discrimination occurs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190">
        <a href="#cite_note-190">
         [190]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Iraq" title="Christianity in Iraq">
        Christians
       </a>
       have lived in the area for about 2,000 years, and many descend from the
       <i>
        pre-Arab
       </i>
       ancient
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesopotamians" title="Mesopotamians">
        Mesopotamians
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">
        Assyrians
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191">
        <a href="#cite_note-191">
         [191]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They numbered over 1.4 million in 1987 or 8% of the estimated population of 16.3 million and 550,000 in 1947 or 12% of the population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192">
        <a href="#cite_note-192">
         [192]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Indigenous
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo_Aramaic" title="Neo Aramaic">
        Neo Aramaic
       </a>
       speaking
       <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">
        Assyrians
       </a>
       , most of whom are adherents of the
       <a href="/wiki/Chaldean_Catholic_Church" title="Chaldean Catholic Church">
        Chaldean Catholic Church
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_Church_of_the_East" title="Assyrian Church of the East">
        Assyrian Church of the East
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_Pentecostal_Church" title="Assyrian Pentecostal Church">
        Assyrian Pentecostal Church
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Syriac_Orthodox_Church" title="Syriac Orthodox Church">
        Syriac Orthodox Church
       </a>
       account for most of the Christian population. Estimates for the numbers of Christians suggest a decline from 8–12% in the mid-20th century to 5% in 2008. More than half of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_Christians" title="Iraqi Christians">
        Iraqi Christians
       </a>
       have fled to neighbouring countries since the start of the war, and many have not returned, although a number are migrating back to the traditional
       <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_homeland" title="Assyrian homeland">
        Assyrian homeland
       </a>
       in the Kurdish Autonomous region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193">
        <a href="#cite_note-193">
         [193]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194">
        <a href="#cite_note-194">
         [194]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There are also small
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethno-religious" title="Ethno-religious">
        ethno-religious
       </a>
       minority populations of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mandaeanism" title="Mandaeanism">
        Mandaeans
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shabaks" title="Shabaks">
        Shabaks
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yarsan" title="Yarsan">
        Yarsan
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yezidi" title="Yezidi">
        Yezidis
       </a>
       remaining. Prior to 2003 their numbers together may have been 2 million, the majority Yarsan, a non-Islamic religion with roots in pre-Islamic and pre-Christian religion. There are reports of over 100.000 conversions to Zoroastrianism in recent years. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_Jewish" title="Iraqi Jewish">
        Iraqi Jewish
       </a>
       community, numbering around 150,000 in 1941, has almost entirely left the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195">
        <a href="#cite_note-195">
         [195]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Iraq is home to two of the world's holiest places among Shias:
       <a href="/wiki/Najaf" title="Najaf">
        Najaf
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Karbala" title="Karbala">
        Karbala
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196">
        <a href="#cite_note-196">
         [196]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Diaspora_and_refugees">
        Diaspora and refugees
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Refugees_of_Iraq" title="Refugees of Iraq">
        Refugees of Iraq
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_exodus_from_Iraq" title="Assyrian exodus from Iraq">
        Assyrian exodus from Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iraqi_Refugees,_Damascus,_Syria.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="714" data-file-width="1000" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Iraqi_Refugees%2C_Damascus%2C_Syria.jpg/220px-Iraqi_Refugees%2C_Damascus%2C_Syria.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Iraqi_Refugees%2C_Damascus%2C_Syria.jpg/330px-Iraqi_Refugees%2C_Damascus%2C_Syria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Iraqi_Refugees%2C_Damascus%2C_Syria.jpg/440px-Iraqi_Refugees%2C_Damascus%2C_Syria.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iraqi_Refugees,_Damascus,_Syria.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Iraqi refugees in
         <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">
          Damascus
         </a>
         , Syria.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The dispersion of native Iraqis to other countries is known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_diaspora" title="Iraqi diaspora">
        Iraqi diaspora
       </a>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_High_Commission_for_Refugees" title="UN High Commission for Refugees">
        UN High Commission for Refugees
       </a>
       has estimated that nearly two million Iraqis have fled the country after the
       <a href="/wiki/Multi-National_Force_%E2%80%93_Iraq" title="Multi-National Force – Iraq">
        multinational
       </a>
       invasion of Iraq in 2003, mostly to
       <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
        Syria
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">
        Jordan
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197">
        <a href="#cite_note-197">
         [197]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Internal Displacement Monitoring Centre estimates an additional 1.9 million are currently displaced within the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198">
        <a href="#cite_note-198">
         [198]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2007, the UN said that about 40% of Iraq's middle class is believed to have fled and that most are fleeing systematic persecution and have no desire to return.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199">
        <a href="#cite_note-199">
         [199]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Refugees are mired in poverty as they are generally barred from working in their host countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200">
        <a href="#cite_note-200">
         [200]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201">
        <a href="#cite_note-201">
         [201]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In recent years the diaspora seems to be returning with the increased security; the Iraqi government claimed that 46,000 refugees have returned to their homes in October 2007 alone.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202">
        <a href="#cite_note-202">
         [202]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As of 2011
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iraq&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , nearly 3 million Iraqis have been displaced, with 1.3 million within Iraq and 1.6 million in neighbouring countries, mainly Jordan and Syria.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203">
        <a href="#cite_note-203">
         [203]
        </a>
       </sup>
       More than half of Iraqi Christians have fled the country since the 2003 US-led invasion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204">
        <a href="#cite_note-204">
         [204]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205">
        <a href="#cite_note-205">
         [205]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to official
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Citizenship_and_Immigration_Services" title="United States Citizenship and Immigration Services">
        United States Citizenship and Immigration Services
       </a>
       statistics, 58,811 Iraqis have been granted refugee-status citizenship as of May 25, 2011.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206">
        <a href="#cite_note-206">
         [206]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       To escape the civil war, over 160,000
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Refugees_of_the_Syrian_civil_war" title="Refugees of the Syrian civil war">
        Syrian refugees
       </a>
       of varying ethnicities have fled to Iraq since 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207">
        <a href="#cite_note-207">
         [207]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Increasing violence during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syrian_civil_war" title="Syrian civil war">
        Syrian civil war
       </a>
       led to an increasing number of Iraqis returning to their native country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208">
        <a href="#cite_note-208">
         [208]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Health">
        Health
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Iraq" title="Health in Iraq">
        Health in Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 2010, spending on healthcare accounted for 6.84% of the country's GDP. In 2008, there were 6.96 physicians and 13.92 nurses per 10,000 inhabitants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209">
        <a href="#cite_note-209">
         [209]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The life expectancy at birth was 68.49 years in 2010, or 65.13 years for males and 72.01 years for females.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210">
        <a href="#cite_note-210">
         [210]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This is down from a peak life expectancy of 71.31 years in 1996.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211">
        <a href="#cite_note-211">
         [211]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Iraq had developed a centralised free health care system in the 1970s using a hospital based, capital-intensive model of
       <a href="/wiki/Curative_care" title="Curative care">
        curative care
       </a>
       . The country depended on large-scale imports of medicines, medical equipment and even nurses, paid for with oil export income, according to a "Watching Brief" report issued jointly by the United Nations Children's Fund (UNICEF) and the World Health Organization (WHO) in July 2003. Unlike other poorer countries, which focused on mass health care using primary care practitioners, Iraq developed a Westernized system of sophisticated hospitals with advanced medical procedures, provided by specialist physicians. The UNICEF/WHO report noted that prior to 1990, 97% of the urban dwellers and 71% of the rural population had access to free primary health care; just 2% of hospital beds were privately managed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-corpwatch_212-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-corpwatch-212">
         [212]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Iraq" title="Education in Iraq">
        Education in Iraq
       </a>
      </div>

          </a>
         </div>
        </td>

           . Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (October 2017)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iraqi_medical_students_at_Basra_University_College_of_Medicine_(2010).JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="5616" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Iraqi_medical_students_at_Basra_University_College_of_Medicine_%282010%29.JPG/220px-Iraqi_medical_students_at_Basra_University_College_of_Medicine_%282010%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Iraqi_medical_students_at_Basra_University_College_of_Medicine_%282010%29.JPG/330px-Iraqi_medical_students_at_Basra_University_College_of_Medicine_%282010%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Iraqi_medical_students_at_Basra_University_College_of_Medicine_%282010%29.JPG/440px-Iraqi_medical_students_at_Basra_University_College_of_Medicine_%282010%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iraqi_medical_students_at_Basra_University_College_of_Medicine_(2010).JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Students at the college of medicine of the
         <a href="/wiki/University_of_Basrah" title="University of Basrah">
          University of Basrah
         </a>
         , 2010.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The CIA World Factbook estimates that, in 2000, the adult
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" title="Literacy rate">
        literacy rate
       </a>
       was 84% for males and 64% for females, with UN figures suggesting a small fall in literacy of Iraqis aged 15–24 between 2000 and 2008, from 84.8% to 82.4%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213">
        <a href="#cite_note-213">
         [213]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Coalition_Provisional_Authority" title="Coalition Provisional Authority">
        Coalition Provisional Authority
       </a>
       undertook a complete reform of Iraq's education system:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baathist" title="Baathist">
        Baathist
       </a>
       ideology was removed from curricula and there were substantial increases in teacher salaries and training programs, which the
       <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">
        Hussein
       </a>
       regime neglected in the 1990s.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       In 2003, an estimated 80% of Iraq's 15,000 school buildings needed rehabilitation and lacked basic sanitary facilities, and most schools lacked libraries and laboratories.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Education is mandatory only through to the sixth grade, after which a national examination determines the possibility of continuing into the upper grades.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Although a vocational track is available to those who do not pass the exam, few students elect that option because of its poor quality.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Boys and girls generally attend separate schools beginning with seventh grade.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2005, obstacles to further reform were poor security conditions in many areas, a centralised system that lacked accountability for teachers and administrators, and the isolation in which the system functioned for the previous 30 years.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Few private schools exist.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Prior to the invasion of 2003, some 240,000 persons were enrolled in institutions of
       <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">
        higher education
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/Webometrics_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Webometrics Ranking of World Universities">
        Webometrics Ranking of World Universities
       </a>
       , the top-ranking universities in the country are the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Dohuk" title="University of Dohuk">
        University of Dohuk
       </a>
       (1717th worldwide), the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Baghdad" title="University of Baghdad">
        University of Baghdad
       </a>
       (3160th) and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Babylon_University" title="Babylon University">
        Babylon University
       </a>
       (3946th).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214">
        <a href="#cite_note-214">
         [214]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Iraq" title="Culture of Iraq">
        Culture of Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Iraq" title="Tourism in Iraq">
        Tourism in Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Iraq" title="Public holidays in Iraq">
        Public holidays in Iraq
       </a>
       include
       <a href="/wiki/Republic_Day" title="Republic Day">
        Republic Day
       </a>
       on 14 July and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Day" title="National Day">
        National Day
       </a>
       on 3 October.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">
        Music
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Iraq" title="Music of Iraq">
        Music of Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Al-Qubanchi.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="858" data-file-width="580" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Al-Qubanchi.jpg/170px-Al-Qubanchi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Al-Qubanchi.jpg/255px-Al-Qubanchi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Al-Qubanchi.jpg/340px-Al-Qubanchi.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Al-Qubanchi.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Iraqi
         <a href="/wiki/Maqam_al-iraqi" title="Maqam al-iraqi">
          maqam
         </a>
         performer Muhammad al-Qubbanchi.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Iraq is known primarily for its rich
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabian_maqam" title="Arabian maqam">
        maqam
       </a>
       heritage which has been passed down orally by the masters of the maqam in an unbroken chain of transmission leading up to the present. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maqam_al-Iraqi" title="Maqam al-Iraqi">
        maqam al-Iraqi
       </a>
       is considered to be the most noble and perfect form of maqam. Al-maqam al-Iraqi is the collection of sung poems written either in one of the sixteen meters of classical Arabic or in Iraqi dialect (Zuhayri).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215">
        <a href="#cite_note-215">
         [215]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This form of art is recognised by UNESCO as "an intangible heritage of humanity".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216">
        <a href="#cite_note-216">
         [216]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Early in the 20th century, many of the most prominent musicians in Iraq were
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jew" title="Jew">
        Jewish
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kojaman_217-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kojaman-217">
         [217]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1936,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Iraq_Radio&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Iraq Radio (page does not exist)">
        Iraq Radio
       </a>
       was established with an ensemble made up entirely of
       <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">
        Jews
       </a>
       , with the exception of the percussion player. At the nightclubs of Baghdad, ensembles consisted of oud, qanun and two percussionists, while the same format with a
       <a href="/wiki/Ney" title="Ney">
        ney
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cello" title="Cello">
        cello
       </a>
       were used on the radio.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kojaman_217-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kojaman-217">
         [217]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The most famous singer of the 1930s–1940s was perhaps the Jew
       <a href="/wiki/Salima_Pasha" title="Salima Pasha">
        Salima Pasha
       </a>
       (later Salima Murad).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kojaman_217-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kojaman-217">
         [217]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manasseh_218-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Manasseh-218">
         [218]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The respect and adoration for Pasha were unusual at the time since public performance by women was considered shameful, and most female singers were recruited from brothels.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kojaman_217-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kojaman-217">
         [217]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The most famous early composer from Iraq was
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ezra_Aharon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ezra Aharon (page does not exist)">
        Ezra Aharon
       </a>
       , an
       <a href="/wiki/Oud" title="Oud">
        oud
       </a>
       player, while the most prominent instrumentalist was
       <a href="/wiki/Saleh_and_Daoud_Al-Kuwaity" title="Saleh and Daoud Al-Kuwaity">
        Daoud Al-Kuwaiti
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Daoud and his brother
       <a href="/wiki/Saleh_and_Daoud_Al-Kuwaity" title="Saleh and Daoud Al-Kuwaity">
        Saleh
       </a>
       formed the official ensemble for the Iraqi radio station and were responsible for introducing the cello and ney into the traditional ensemble.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kojaman_217-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kojaman-217">
         [217]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Art_and_architecture">
        Art and architecture
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ancient_ziggurat_at_Ali_Air_Base_Iraq_2005.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1932" data-file-width="2576" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Ancient_ziggurat_at_Ali_Air_Base_Iraq_2005.jpg/220px-Ancient_ziggurat_at_Ali_Air_Base_Iraq_2005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Ancient_ziggurat_at_Ali_Air_Base_Iraq_2005.jpg/330px-Ancient_ziggurat_at_Ali_Air_Base_Iraq_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Ancient_ziggurat_at_Ali_Air_Base_Iraq_2005.jpg/440px-Ancient_ziggurat_at_Ali_Air_Base_Iraq_2005.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ancient_ziggurat_at_Ali_Air_Base_Iraq_2005.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Ziggurat_of_Ur" title="Great Ziggurat of Ur">
          Great Ziggurat of Ur
         </a>
         near
         <a href="/wiki/Nasiriyah" title="Nasiriyah">
          Nasiriyah
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Mesopotamia" title="Architecture of Mesopotamia">
        Architecture of Mesopotamia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_art" title="Iraqi art">
        Iraqi art
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Important cultural institutions in the capital include the
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_National_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Iraqi National Symphony Orchestra">
        Iraqi National Symphony Orchestra
       </a>
       – rehearsals and performances were briefly interrupted during the
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iraq_(2003%E2%80%932011)" title="History of Iraq (2003–2011)">
        Occupation of Iraq
       </a>
       but have since returned to normal. The National Theatre of Iraq was looted during the 2003 invasion, but efforts are underway to restore it. The live theatre scene received a boost during the 1990s when UN sanctions limited the import of foreign films. As many as 30 cinemas were reported to have been converted to live stages, producing a wide range of comedies and dramatic productions.
      </p>
      <p>
       Institutions offering cultural education in Baghdad include the Academy of Music, Institute of Fine Arts and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_and_Ballet_school_Baghdad" title="Music and Ballet school Baghdad">
        Music and Ballet school Baghdad
       </a>
       . Baghdad also features a number of museums including the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Iraq" title="National Museum of Iraq">
        National Museum of Iraq
       </a>
       – which houses the world's largest and finest collection of artefacts and relics of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Iraq" title="Ancient Iraq">
        Ancient Iraqi
       </a>
       civilisations; some of which were
       <a href="/wiki/Archaeological_looting_in_Iraq" title="Archaeological looting in Iraq">
        stolen
       </a>
       during the
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iraq_(2003%E2%80%932011)" title="History of Iraq (2003–2011)">
        Occupation of Iraq
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hatra-109728.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1173" data-file-width="2023" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Hatra-109728.jpg/220px-Hatra-109728.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Hatra-109728.jpg/330px-Hatra-109728.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Hatra-109728.jpg/440px-Hatra-109728.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hatra-109728.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Facade of Temple at Hatra, declared
         <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
          World Heritage Site
         </a>
         by
         <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
          UNESCO
         </a>
         in 1985.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The capital, Ninus or
       <a href="/wiki/Nineveh" title="Nineveh">
        Nineveh
       </a>
       , was taken by the
       <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">
        Medes
       </a>
       under
       <a href="/wiki/Cyaxares" title="Cyaxares">
        Cyaxares
       </a>
       , and some 200 years after
       <a href="/wiki/Xenophon" title="Xenophon">
        Xenophon
       </a>
       passed over its site, then mere mounds of earth. It remained buried until 1845, when Botta and Layard discovered the ruins of the Assyrian cities. The principal remains are those of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khorsabad" title="Khorsabad">
        Khorsabad
       </a>
       , 16 km (10 mi) N.E. of
       <a href="/wiki/Mosul" title="Mosul">
        Mosul
       </a>
       ; of Nimroud, supposed to be the ancient Calah; and of Kouyunjik, in all probability the ancient Nineveh. In these cities are found fragments of several great buildings which seem to have been palace-temples. They were constructed chiefly of
       <a href="/wiki/Mudbrick" title="Mudbrick">
        sun-dried bricks
       </a>
       , and all that remains of them is the lower part of the walls, decorated with sculpture and paintings, portions of the pavements, a few indications of the elevation, and some interesting works connected with the drainage.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
        Media
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Iraq" title="Media of Iraq">
        Media of Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       After the end of the full state control in 2003, there were a period of significant growth in the broadcast media in Iraq. Immediately, and the ban on satellite dishes is no longer in place, and by mid-2003, according to a
       <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">
        BBC
       </a>
       report, there were 20 radio stations from 0.15 to 17 television stations owned by Iraqis, and 200 Iraqi newspapers owned and operated. Significantly, there have been many of these newspapers in numbers disproportionate to the population of their locations. For example, in
       <a href="/wiki/Najaf" title="Najaf">
        Najaf
       </a>
       , which has a population of 300,000, is being published more than 30 newspapers and distributed.
      </p>
      <p>
       Iraqi media expert and author of a number of reports on this subject, Ibrahim Al Marashi, identifies four stages of the US invasion of Iraq in 2003 where they had been taking the steps that have significant effects on the way for the later of the Iraqi media since then. Stages are: pre-invasion preparation, and the war and the actual choice of targets, the first post-war period, and a growing insurgency and hand over power to the Iraqi Interim Government (IIG) and Prime Minister
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iyad_Allawi" title="Iyad Allawi">
        Iyad Allawi
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219">
        <a href="#cite_note-219">
         [219]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
          <span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (March 2013)">
           page needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">
        Cuisine
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_cuisine" title="Iraqi cuisine">
        Iraqi cuisine
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Masgouf,_an_Iraqi_tradition_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Masgouf%2C_an_Iraqi_tradition_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/220px-Masgouf%2C_an_Iraqi_tradition_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Masgouf%2C_an_Iraqi_tradition_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/330px-Masgouf%2C_an_Iraqi_tradition_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Masgouf%2C_an_Iraqi_tradition_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/440px-Masgouf%2C_an_Iraqi_tradition_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Masgouf,_an_Iraqi_tradition_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Masgouf" title="Masgouf">
          Masgouf
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Iraqi cuisine can be traced back some 10,000 years – to the
       <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">
        Sumerians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Akkadian_Empire" title="Akkadian Empire">
        Akkadians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">
        Babylonians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">
        Assyrians
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">
        Ancient Persians
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Salloum_220-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Salloum-220">
         [220]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Clay_tablet" title="Clay tablet">
        Tablets
       </a>
       found in ancient ruins in Iraq show recipes prepared in the temples during religious festivals – the first cookbooks in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Salloum_220-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Salloum-220">
         [220]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Iraq" title="Ancient Iraq">
        Ancient Iraq
       </a>
       , or
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">
         Mesopotamia
        </a>
       </i>
       , was home to many sophisticated and highly advanced civilisations, in all fields of knowledge – including the culinary arts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Salloum_220-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Salloum-220">
         [220]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, it was in the
       <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">
        medieval era
       </a>
       when Baghdad was the capital of the
       <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">
        Abbasid Caliphate
       </a>
       that the Iraqi kitchen reached its zenith.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Salloum_220-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Salloum-220">
         [220]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Today the cuisine of Iraq reflects this rich inheritance as well as strong influences from the culinary traditions of neighbouring
       <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
        Turkey
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">
        Iran
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Syria" title="Greater Syria">
        Greater Syria
       </a>
       area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Salloum_220-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Salloum-220">
         [220]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Some characteristic ingredients of Iraqi cuisine include – vegetables such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aubergine" title="Aubergine">
        aubergine
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">
        tomato
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Okra" title="Okra">
        okra
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Onion" title="Onion">
        onion
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">
        potato
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Courgette" title="Courgette">
        courgette
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Garlic" title="Garlic">
        garlic
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bell_pepper" title="Bell pepper">
        peppers
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Chili_pepper" title="Chili pepper">
        chilli
       </a>
       , cereals such as
       <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">
        rice
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bulgur" title="Bulgur">
        bulgur
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">
        wheat
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">
        barley
       </a>
       , pulses and legumes such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lentils" title="Lentils">
        lentils
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chickpeas" title="Chickpeas">
        chickpeas
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cannellini#White_beans" title="Cannellini">
        cannellini
       </a>
       , fruits such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Date_Palm#Dates" title="Date Palm">
        dates
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Raisin" title="Raisin">
        raisins
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Apricot" title="Apricot">
        apricots
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Common_fig" title="Common fig">
        figs
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Grape" title="Grape">
        grapes
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Melon" title="Melon">
        melon
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pomegranate" title="Pomegranate">
        pomegranate
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Citrus" title="Citrus">
        citrus fruits
       </a>
       , especially
       <a href="/wiki/Lemon" title="Lemon">
        lemon
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lime_(fruit)" title="Lime (fruit)">
        lime
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Salloum_220-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-Salloum-220">
         [220]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Similarly with other countries of
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">
        Western Asia
       </a>
       , chicken and especially lamb are the favourite meats. Most dishes are served with rice – usually
       <a href="/wiki/Basmati" title="Basmati">
        Basmati
       </a>
       , grown in the
       <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamian_Marshes" title="Mesopotamian Marshes">
        marshes
       </a>
       of southern Iraq.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Salloum_220-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-Salloum-220">
         [220]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Bulgur" title="Bulgur">
        Bulgur
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">
        wheat
       </a>
       is used in many dishes – having been a staple in the country since the days of the
       <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">
        Ancient Assyrians
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Salloum_220-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-Salloum-220">
         [220]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">
        Sport
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Iraq" title="Sport in Iraq">
        Sport in Iraq
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">
        Football
       </a>
       is the most popular sport in Iraq. Football is a considerable uniting factor in Iraq following years of war and unrest.
       <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">
        Basketball
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">
        swimming
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Olympic_weightlifting" title="Olympic weightlifting">
        weightlifting
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bodybuilding" title="Bodybuilding">
        bodybuilding
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">
        boxing
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kick_boxing" title="Kick boxing">
        kick boxing
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">
        tennis
       </a>
       are also popular sports.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_Football_Association" title="Iraqi Football Association">
        Iraqi Football Association
       </a>
       is the governing body of football in Iraq, controlling the
       <a href="/wiki/Iraq_national_football_team" title="Iraq national football team">
        Iraqi National Team
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Premier_League" title="Iraqi Premier League">
        Iraqi Premier League
       </a>
       (also known as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dawri_Al-Nokba" title="Dawri Al-Nokba">
        Dawri Al-Nokba
       </a>
       ). It was founded in 1948, and has been a member of
       <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">
        FIFA
       </a>
       since 1950 and the
       <a href="/wiki/Asian_Football_Confederation" title="Asian Football Confederation">
        Asian Football Confederation
       </a>
       since 1971. The biggest club in Iraq is
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Shorta_SC" title="Al-Shorta SC">
        Al-Shorta
       </a>
       , who won back-to-back league titles in 2013 and 2014 and were the first ever winners of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_Champions_League" title="Arab Champions League">
        Arab Champions League
       </a>
       . The Iraqi National Football Team were the
       <a href="/wiki/2007_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2007 AFC Asian Cup">
        2007 AFC Asian Cup
       </a>
       champions after defeating
       <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">
        Saudi Arabia
       </a>
       in the final by 1–0 thanks to a goal by captain
       <a href="/wiki/Younis_Mahmoud" title="Younis Mahmoud">
        Younis Mahmoud
       </a>
       and they have participated in two
       <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">
        FIFA
       </a>
       competitions (the
       <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">
        1986 FIFA World Cup
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/2009_FIFA_Confederations_Cup" title="2009 FIFA Confederations Cup">
        2009 FIFA Confederations Cup
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">
        Technology
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_phones">
        Mobile phones
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Despite having mobile phones in the Middle East since 1995, Iraqis were only able to use mobile phones after 2003. Mobile phones were banned under Saddam's rule. In 2013, it was reported that 78% of Iraqis owned a mobile phone.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221">
        <a href="#cite_note-221">
         [221]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Satellite">
        Satellite
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       According to the Iraqi Ministry of Communication, Iraq is now in the second phase of building and launching a multipurpose strategic satellite.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222">
        <a href="#cite_note-222">
         [222]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A project which expected to cost $600 million is ongoing in co-operation with market leaders such as
       <a href="/wiki/Astrium" title="Astrium">
        Astrium
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Arianespace" title="Arianespace">
        Arianespace
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Undersea_cable">
        Undersea cable
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On 18 January 2012, Iraq was connected to the undersea communications network for the first time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223">
        <a href="#cite_note-223">
         [223]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       This had an immense impact on internet speed, availability and usage in Iraq.
      </p>
      <p>
       In October 2013, the Iraqi Minister for Communication ordered internet prices to be lowered by a third. This is an attempt to boost usage and comes as a result of significant improvements in Internet infrastructure in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224">
        <a href="#cite_note-224">
         [224]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

        <li id="cite_note-10">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-10">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation web">
           Halloran, John A. (2000).
           <a class="external text" href="http://sumerian.org/sumerlex.htm" rel="nofollow">
            "Sumerian Lexicon"
           </a>
           .
           <q>
            The name of the very ancient city of URUK- City of Gilgamesh is made up from the UR-city and UK- thought to mean existence (a-ku, a-Ki &amp; a-ko. The Aramaic and Arabic root of IRQ and URQ denotes rivers or tributaries at the same times referring to condensation (of water).
           </q>
          </cite>

           <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Wilson" title="Jeremy Wilson">
            Wilson, Jeremy
           </a>
           (1998).
           <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/?id=OsEhAQAAIAAJ&amp;q=%22Lawrence+of+Arabia%22&amp;dq=%22Lawrence+of+Arabia%22" rel="nofollow">

            </i>
           </a>

            ISBN

           </a>

           <q>
            The exploits of T.E. Lawrence as British liaison officer in the Arab Revolt, recounted in his work Seven Pillars of Wisdom, made him one of the most famous Englishmen of his generation. This biography explores his life and career including his correspondence with writers, artists and politicians.
           </q>
